In re Lewkowitz


No. 5235


Supreme Court of Arizona


69 Ariz. 347; 213 P.2d 690; 1950 Ariz. LEXIS 266



January 16, 1950, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motions granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents filed motions to vacate, quash, and dismiss an order to show cause directed against respondents in an action brought by petitioner Arizona State Bar.


OVERVIEW: An order to show cause was directed against respondents in an action brought by the State Bar. Respondents filed motions to vacate, quash, and dismiss the order alleging that the title to the Arizona State Bar Act, Ariz. Code Ann. § 32-301 et seq. (1939), was insufficient to meet the requirements of Ariz. Const. art. 4, § 13, pt. 2, insofar as the provisions of the State Bar Act dealt with rules of professional conduct, disbarment and discipline, breach of rules, local administrative committees, and proceedings and procedure of disbarment. The court granted the motions to quash and dismiss the order. The court held that Ariz. Code Ann. §§ 32-329, 32-335, 32-337, 32-338, 32-339, and 32-340 (1939) were unconstitutional and void. The title under which the State Bar Act was enacted was too restricted to authorize the broad powers granted to the Arizona State Bar under the provisions of the act related to the discipline, suspension, and disbarment of attorneys. The matters were not germane or directly or indirectly related to the subject of the title and had no natural connection to it. No one reading the title could logically infer that the provisions would be incorporated in the act.


OUTCOME: The court granted respondents' motions to quash and dismiss the order to show cause directed against them.

645 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Maricopa County v. Douglas


No. 4998


Supreme Court of Arizona


69 Ariz. 35; 208 P.2d 646; 1949 Ariz. LEXIS 85



July 18, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, Maricopa County; M. T. Phelps, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded with instructions to enter judgment for plaintiff in conformity with opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Maricopa County (Arizona) that refused to order defendants, daughter and son-in-law, to return funds paid to the recipient of old-age assistance under the public welfare law.


OVERVIEW: The county filed an action against defendants for return of funds paid to the recipient for old-age assistance under the public welfare law. Judgment was rendered for defendants on the ground that the law was unconstitutional. The court reversed. The law was not unconstitutionally vague where only the county attorney, the party that instituted the action, was authorized to satisfy the judgment lien of record. The law, which required adult children of old-age recipients to refund assistance paid, established a reasonable classification under the Equal Protection Clause because the number of needy blind that received assistance hardly compared to the number that received old age assistance, and the obligation to pay for the maintenance of certain relatives did not in itself constitute double taxation. Because the statute did not include a "son-in-law," only a judgment for a separate debt against the daughter could have been found. Such a judgment was not recoverable out of defendants' community property because public policy favored the maintenance of the community over the support of the aged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that refused to order defendants to return funds paid to the recipient of old-age assistance under the public welfare law.

 

646 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Maricopa County Mun. Water Conservation Dist. v. Warford


No. 5104


Supreme Court of Arizona


69 Ariz. 1; 206 P.2d 1168; 1949 Ariz. LEXIS 80



May 31, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 16, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court, Maricopa County; Edwin Beauchamp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant water district challenged a judgment of the Superior Court, Maricopa County (Arizona), which found in favor of plaintiff landowner. The landowner brought an action for inverse eminent domain, Ariz. Const. art. II, § 17, after waters came down the water district's artificially created diversion channel and flooded his land and damaged his crops.


OVERVIEW: The court found that it was unnecessary for the landowner to comply with the statutes governing verified claims, which did not apply to eminent domain liability. The court found that the right of property in the individual and to damages for its taking existed long prior to the adoption of the state constitution, so it was not a liability created by statute to which the one-year statute of limitations applied. The court found that the water district's method by which it attempted to use and take the land must necessarily be by prescription, because it had neither purchased nor condemned it under eminent domain. The court concluded that no amount of delay short of the prescriptive period of 10 years would defeat the landowner's action for compensation. The court found that the fact that the landowner still had his property was no satisfaction for his damages, because a taking of any kind or an infringement on the use of his property that diminished its value in whole or in part was a compensable loss. The court concluded that the measure of damages was the depreciation in the market value of the whole tract and that damage to crops was to be taken into consideration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Hernandez v. Frohmiller


No. 5202


Supreme Court of Arizona


68 Ariz. 242; 204 P.2d 854; 1949 Ariz. LEXIS 133



April 4, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus proceeding by Filomena Hernandez against Ana Frohmiller, State Auditor of the State of Arizona, to require respondent to allow claim of petitioner and to draw a warrant in favor of petitioner for wages due petitioner for personal services rendered to the state, wherein Roy Hislop and others, constituting the Arizona State Civil Service Board, intervened.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner contended that a state civil service act was unconstitutional and void, thus respondent, a state auditor, is obligated to draw a warrant in petitioner's favor on the treasurer of the state for wages due for personal services rendered to the state.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was granted of writ of mandamus commanding respondent, as auditor of the state, to draw a warrant in petitioner's favor on the treasurer of the state for wages due petitioner for personal services rendered to the state. The auditor declined and argued that the act would be in violation of a state civil service act. The court held that the act was unconstitutional because if the statute were given effect every political subdivision of the state would come under the supervision of the state board appointed by the governor. Further, the court determined that the act violated Ariz. Const. art. XI, § 2, by granting supervision of state educational institutions to the civil service board. Moreover, the court held that the act was incapable of intelligent enforcement, delegated legislative authority to the civil service board, and it lacked a legal basis for imposing greater burdens on first class counties.


OUTCOME: Court held that the civil service act was unconstitutional because the title of the act makes no reference to political subdivisions of the state except the counties, was incapable of intelligent enforcement, improperly delegated legislative powers and lacked a legal basis for imposing greater burdens on first class counties.

Ex parte Riccardi


No. 5023


Supreme Court of Arizona


68 Ariz. 180; 203 P.2d 627; 1949 Ariz. LEXIS 123



March 7, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, Cochise County.

Proceeding in the matter of the application of Constantino Vincent Riccardi, also known as C. Vincent Riccardi, for a writ of habeas corpus. From an order discharging petitioner from custody under extradition warrant, the State of Arizona appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Arizona, sought review of an order the Superior Court, Cochise County (Arizona) that granted petitioner inmate a writ of habeas corpus and discharged him from custody under an extradition warrant that had been issued by the Governor of Arizona at the request of the Governor of New York.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus upon finding that there was no evidence that he had been in New York at the time of the commission of the offense. The trial court also found that the extradition warrant contained a fatal defect, in that no warrant from a New York court was with the extradition documents presented to the Governor of Arizona. On appeal, the court held that the extradition warrant recited ample jurisdictional facts establishing that the inmate was a fugitive from justice and was prima facie evidence thereof. The court found that the evidence submitted to the trial court by the inmate was at best only contradictory of the substantial evidence presented by the State. The court held void that part of Ariz. Code Ann. § 44-3606, which required a warrant on the affidavit because that requirement conflicted with 18 U.S.C.S. § 3182, which provided that a warrant on the indictment or on any other form of criminal charge was not necessary in an extradition proceeding. Despite several errors, the court found nothing indicating that any document in the extradition papers was spurious, or in any way affected the inmate's rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

Goodwin v. Superior Court


No. 5179


Supreme Court of Arizona


68 Ariz. 108; 201 P.2d 124; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 86



December 27, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 10, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original application for writ of prohibition by M. A. Goodwin, Superintendent of the Division of Motor Vehicles, Arizona State Highway Department, applicant, against the Superior Court of Yavapai County, State of Arizona, and W. E. Patterson, Judge of the Superior Court of Yavapai County, Arizona, respondents, to prohibit respondents from proceeding with a certain action brought to review the applicant's action in revoking a chauffeur's license. On motion by respondents to dismiss.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied and alternative writ of prohibition made peremptory.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was a motion by respondents, the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona) and a judge of that court, to dismiss an original application for a writ of prohibition by applicant, the Superintendent of the Division of Motor Vehicles, Arizona State Highway Department, to prohibit respondents from proceeding with a certain action brought to review the Superintendent's action in revoking a chauffeur's license.


OVERVIEW: The Superintendent filed an original application for a writ of prohibition asking that an alternative writ of prohibition be issued to respondents to prohibit them from proceeding with an action pending in respondent court that was instituted by a driver against the Superintendent, alleging that after he plead guilty in Nebraska to a charge of driving under the influence (DUI) and was fined, the Superintendent, without notice, due process, or authority, revoked the driver's chauffeur's license. The Superintendent filed a motion for summary judgment, which was denied, and it appeared that respondent judge would proceed to try the case unless the court ordered otherwise by writ of prohibition. Respondents filed a motion to dismiss, which the court denied and made the alternative writ of prohibition peremptory. The driver was given the opportunity in Nebraska to be heard and to disprove the charge, and by pleading guilty he had to accept all of the burdens and disabilities that flowed from the Nebraska conviction. It was undoubtedly the intention of the legislature to keep those convicted of DUI off the Arizona highways, whether their offense was committed within or without Arizona.


OUTCOME: The court denied respondents' motion to dismiss and made peremptory the alternative writ of prohibition.

 

650 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pelosi


No. 981


Supreme Court of Arizona


68 Ariz. 51; 199 P.2d 125; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 79



November 8, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, Maricopa County; H. C. Kelly, Judge.

Frank Pelosi, Joe Dean Davis, and Irvin Kaslow were convicted of violating statute making betting on result of a horse race illegal, and they appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted them of illegally receiving bets on a result of a horse race.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with being bookies and taking illegal bets on a horse race. A temporary restraining order was issued to prevent defendants from taking bets. The attorney general and several others went to serve the order. While serving the order, defendants were seen taking bets and were arrested. No arrest warrants had been issued. The police seized several items that bookies commonly used in running their operations. Defendants unsuccessfully filed motions to suppress. Defendants were convicted. Motions for a new trial and arrest of judgment were denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the information that charged that defendant took money on a race that was to be run was not insufficient. It did not matter whether the race was actually conducted. The prohibition in Ariz. Code Ann. § 73-1607a (Cum. Supp. 1939) of "placing or making a bet or wager" also necessarily encompassed the receiving of the bet. By receiving the bet, the bookie was also betting that the person making the bet would lose. The court found that the seizure of evidence was not illegal because the police were lawfully serving the order and a crime was being conducted in front of them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

652 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allred


No. 5004


Supreme Court of Arizona


67 Ariz. 320; 195 P.2d 163; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 127; 4 A.L.R.2d 735



June 17, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, Maricopa County; M. T. Phelps, Judge.

Suit by James B. Allred against the State of Arizona, a body politic and others, and B. F. Youngker and C. O. Vosburg. B. F. Youngker and C. O. Vosburgh filed a cross-claim. From the judgment, the State of Arizona and others appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the State and county officials, challenged the judgment by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found in favor of appellee veteran in his action for clear title to property.


OVERVIEW: The veteran owned real property. He claimed the exemption for property taxes which was available to veterans, pursuant to Ariz. Const. art. IX, § 2 for several years, but failed to claim the exemption for 1932. The veteran did not pay the 1932 taxes, and the property was sold by the county. When the veteran learned of the sale, he tendered the taxes which were allegedly due, but the county refused to accept them. In the meantime, the property was sold to the purchasers. The veteran filed an action for clear title to the property. The purchasers filed a cross-claim for reimbursement of the purchase price. The trial court found in favor of the veteran and the purchasers. On the State and county officials appeal, the court reversed. Pursuant to Ariz. Code Ann. § 73-303 (1939), anyone entitled to a veteran's exemption was required to make application for that exemption each year. The failure to make application was deemed a waiver, pursuant to Ariz. Code Ann. § 73-304. Even though the constitutional provision was self-executing, the legislature had the power to set up a reasonable procedure by which the exemption was to be exercised.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had found in favor of the veteran in his action for title to property. The case was remanded for dismissal of the veteran's action.

 

653 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Barrows v. Garvey


No. 5110


Supreme Court of Arizona


67 Ariz. 202; 193 P.2d 913; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 113



May 24, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceedings in mandamus by Earle F. Barrows against Dan E. Garvey, as Secretary of State of the State of Arizona, to compel defendant to remove and delete from a notice prepared by him the names of the offices of justice of the peace and constables of the several justice precincts of Maricopa county.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ made peremptory.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen brought an original proceeding in the court for a mandamus against respondent Secretary of State of the State of Arizona, to compel the Secretary to remove and delete from a notice prepared by the Secretary pursuant to Ariz. Code Ann. § 55-1002 (1939) the names of the offices of justice of the peace and constables of the several justice precincts in a county.


OVERVIEW: The citizen claimed that the elections for constable and justice of the peace were not to be held at the election for which the Secretary was placing their names on the ballot, since their terms were not expiring, and the Secretary claimed that Ariz. Const. art. 7, § 11 limited the term of office for the justice of the peace to two years, which could not be changed by the legislature. The court determined that § 11 did not set the length of the term for justices of the peace, but only set the time for the elections. The court also determined that the office of constable was created by the legislature, so it was regulated by the legislature. The court held that the length of the term for a constable and a justice of the peace was regulated by the legislature and the enactment by the legislature of 1945 Ariz. Laws ch. 69 (Ariz. Code Ann. § 17-504 (as amended 1939)) was a valid enactment and did not violate any provisions of the Arizona Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the alternative writ was made peremptory.

Arizona Corp. Comm'n v. Tucson Gas, Elec. Light & Power Co.


No. 5042


Supreme Court of Arizona


67 Ariz. 12; 189 P.2d 907; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 90



February 20, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, Maricopa County; M. T. Phelps, Judge.

Suit by the Tucson Gas, Electric Light & Power Company, a corporation, against the Arizona Corporation Commission, and Wilson T. Wright and others, as members of and constituting the Arizona Corporation Commission, to set aside and annul certain orders of the commission. From a judgment vacating the commission's orders, the commission and its members appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with instructions to sustain motion to dismiss complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Arizona Corporation Commission (commission), challenged a judgment of the Superior Court, Maricopa County (Arizona), which vacated the commission's orders, that had, pursuant to Ariz. Code Ann. § 27-916 (1939), required appellee public utility to make capital additions, improvements, and extensions necessary to serve parties that had applied for utility services. The superior court held that the orders were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 27-916, the commission had ordered the public utility to make capital additions, improvements, and extensions necessary to serve parties that had applied for utility service. The commission did not construe the constitutionality of § 27-916. The superior court vacated the commission's orders upon the grounds that the orders resulted in taking property without just compensation and without due process of law, and were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed and instructed that the public utility's complaint be dismissed. The court held that the condemnation procedure provided for in § 27-916, was unconstitutional as applied to the taking of property of public utilities. The procedure was inadequate as a means of assessing he compensation to be paid to the public utility. However, the court concluded that the commission's orders were valid and within the jurisdiction of the commission. The public utility was under the duty and subject to the orders of the commission to make such extensions, improvements, and betterments as may be required to render adequate service to the communities it served, Ariz. Const. art. 15, § 3; Ariz. Code Ann. § 69-222 (1939).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which had vacated the commission's orders. The court remanded with instructions to sustain the motion to dismiss the public utility's complaint. The court concluded that the commission's orders, which required the public utility to make capital improvements in order to provide service to parties that had applied for utility service, were valid.

 

655 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


AMERICAN FEDN. OF LABOR v. AMERICAN SASH & DOOR CO.


No. 5028


Supreme Court of Arizona


67 Ariz. 20; 189 P.2d 912; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 91; 21 L.R.R.M. 2311; 14 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P64,293



February 4, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, Maricopa County; M. T. Phelps, Judge.

Proceeding by American Federation of Labor, Arizona State Federation of Labor, Phoenix Building & Construction Trades Council, United Brotherhood of Carpenters and Joiners of America, Millmen, Cabinet Makers and Lumber Handlers Union No. 2093, Forest L. Stiers individually and as president of Local Union No. 2093, and Ralph Henley, doing business as Ralph Henley Millwork, against American Sash & Door Company, a corporation, D. A. Brewer, W. B. Stevens, Edward L. Beard, James R. Miller, and John L. Sullivan, individually and as Attorney General of the State of Arizona (succeeded by Evo De Concini as Attorney General, who has been substituted as a party defendant), for a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of the "right to work" amendment to the Arizona Constitution. From the judgment, plaintiffs appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant labor organizations challenged the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted appellee attorney general's motion to dismiss the labor organizations' complaint, which sought relief on federal constitutional grounds from an amendment to the state constitution that established one's right not to join a union.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the labor organizations contended that their complaint was improperly dismissed because the state constitutional amendment that gave workers the right to non-union membership violated the federal Constitution. The attorney general countered that the amendment did not impair contractual obligations or violate the Fifth, Fourteenth, or First Amendments. The court affirmed the lower court's grant of the attorney general's motion to dismiss the labor organizations' complaint. The court held that the exercise of the state's police power in adopting the presumptively constitutional amendment was not so unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious as to be unconstitutional. The labor organizations failed to meet their burden of showing that the amendment was irrational and did not contribute to the public health, safety, and welfare. Nor did the amendment impair the rights of free speech and assembly because it protected the rights of workers to choose whether or not to become union members. Also, the amendment did not retrospectively alter existing contracts. In addition to the foregoing, the judicial power was limited to an assessment of the amendment's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's grant of the attorney general's motion to dismiss the labor organizations' complaint, which challenged the constitutionality of an amendment to the state constitution that gave workers the right not to join unions.

 

656 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Ethington v. Wright


No. 4981


Supreme Court of Arizona


66 Ariz. 382; 189 P.2d 209; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 143



January 26, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, Maricopa County; Dudley W. Windes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county taxpayers appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted the motion to dismiss of defendants, members of the Corporation Commission of the State of Arizona (commission), Auditor of the State of Arizona, and Attorney General of the State of Arizona, in a class action by the taxpayers alleging the unconstitutionality of 1945 Ariz. Sess. Laws 11 (Act).


OVERVIEW: The state enacted the Act, which levied taxes on real and personal property in the state, including property owned by the taxpayers. The taxpayers brought a class action against defendants, alleging that portions of the Act were unconstitutional and seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. The lower court granted defendants' motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the taxpayers had a right to challenge the Act because they were financially affected by it, in that taxes were levied on their property to raise funds that they alleged would be spent illegally in paying the Federal Power Commission (FPC) to assist the commission in a rate survey to establish a rate base. The Act was held unconstitutional under Ariz. Const. arts. 3, 15; and U.S. Const. amend. X because while it was not illegal for the commission, as a state agency, to use the FPC's services on a rate survey, the commission had been created under Ariz. Const. art. 15 and thus the legislature could not force upon the commission a particular mode of accomplishing its constitutional duties as defined under art. 15.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting defendants' motion to dismiss and directed the lower court to deny such motion and enter judgment in favor of the taxpayers.

State ex rel. De Concini v. Sullivan


No. 5058


Supreme Court of Arizona


66 Ariz. 348; 188 P.2d 592; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 139



January 10, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Quo warranto proceedings, on the relation of Evo De Concini, Attorney General of the State of Arizona, against John L. Sullivan, respondent, for a judgment excluding the respondent from the office of Attorney General.



DISPOSITION: Judgment rendered excluding respondent from office of Attorney General.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An original action in quo warranto was filed pursuant to Ariz. Const. art. 6, § 4 and Ariz. Code Ann. § 28-301 in the name of petitioner state upon the relation of an individual claiming to be the state attorney general against respondent, purported attorney general, who was alleged to be usurping the office. The court issued a citation directing respondent to answer by what warrant he claimed to exercise the office of attorney general.


OVERVIEW: Respondent while attorney general was found guilty on two counts of an information charging him with the crime of conspiracy to violate the gambling laws of the state and was sentenced to a term of imprisonment. The governor, upon notification of the judgment of conviction, appointed relator to the office. Relator alleged that respondent refused to be ousted from office and thereafter the state filed an action in quo warranto, pursuant to Ariz. Const. art. 6, § 4 and Ariz. Code Ann. § 28-301(1939), seeking a judgment on the issue. Upon review, the court held that respondent was ousted from office. The court ruled that Ariz. Code Ann. § 12-404, the provision defining when an office would be deemed vacant, which included the happening of an incumbent's conviction of a felony, or of any offense involving a violation of his official duties, was constitutional as a safeguard to the public against those who breached its trust and that its express provisions created a vacancy in the office of attorney general upon the conviction of respondent. The court held that, since the date of respondent's conviction, respondent was unlawfully usurping, intruding into, and holding the office.


OUTCOME: The court declared that respondent was excluded from the office of attorney general for the remainder of the term.

Supreme Court of Arizona


66 Ariz. 339; 188 P.2d 457; 1948 Ariz. LEXIS 138



January 5, 1948

OVERVIEW: The CPA entered into a contract with the commission to make an examination of certain public service corporations operating in Arizona. The data to be thus procured by the CPA and his assistants was to be used by the commission in connection with the performance of the duties imposed on it under Ariz. Const. art. XV, § 3, i. e., making classifications, rates, and charges of public utilities. The CPA filed a declaratory judgment action, and the trial court granted the auditor's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court because there was no appropriation of funds that was directed to the commission for the payment of its obligations. The statutes claimed by the CPA to fund his claims were not severable and applied to specific services not provided by the CPA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the state auditor's motion for summary judgment in the CPA's action for a declaratory judgment to determine the question as to whether any funds were available for the payment of the CPA's claim for services rendered to the commission.

Pima County v. Hogan


2 CA-CV 99-0065


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


197 Ariz. 138; 3 P.3d 1058; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 212; 309 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



November 30, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED by Arizona Supreme Court September 26, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 307026. Honorable Robert Donfeld, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county appealed the order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), denying its request for sanctions against defendant landowner under Ariz. R. Civ. P. 68 after a bench trial in an eminent domain action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county brought an eminent domain action against defendant landowner pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1116 for road construction. Following a bench trial, the court awarded defendant $ 27,890 for the parcel condemned, plus taxable costs. Plaintiff then moved, pursuant to Ariz. R. Civ. P. 68, for sanctions because the award was more favorable to it than its pretrial offer. The trial court denied plaintiff's motion. On appeal, plaintiff contended that the trial court erred when it found that Ariz. R. Civ. P. 68 did not apply to eminent domain proceedings. The court found a direct conflict between the rule and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1128, which gave the court discretion to apportion costs. Since mandatory cost allocation in eminent domain proceedings implicated a substantive constitutional right, the trial court did not err in finding Ariz. R. Civ. P. 68 did not apply to eminent domain proceedings.


OUTCOME: Order denying plaintiff's request for sanctions affirmed because the trial court did not err in refusing to apply the mandatory cost allocation rule.

 

660 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Cesar R.


2 CA-JV 99-0034


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


197 Ariz. 437; 4 P.3d 980; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 213; 309 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 36



November 30, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 12196403. Honorable Jim D. Himelic, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Minor appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) adjudicating him delinquent on one count of a minor in possession of a firearm, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3111, for firing four shots into the air in a residential neighborhood. Minor challenged the constitutionality of § 13-3111.


OVERVIEW: Minor fired four shots into the air in a residential neighborhood. The juvenile court adjudicated him delinquent under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3111, minor in possession of a firearm, and disorderly conduct. Under § 13-3111(H), application was limited to counties with populations of more than 500,000 persons. Minor argued that this limitation violated Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 19. The court held that: (1) there was a legitimate legislative purpose: regulating a minor's possession and use of firearms; (2) rather than encompassing all members of the relevant class, it applied to juveniles in the two most populated counties only; (3) the class created was insufficiently elastic: it was only theoretical, not probable that counties' populations would shift enough for others to enter or exit the class; and therefore, (4) § 13-3111 was unconstitutional. The court declined to sever the subsection limiting application to more populated counties.


OUTCOME: Finding vacated; minor in possession of firearm statute was unconstitutional because instead of applying to all juveniles, it applied only to juveniles in the two most populated counties and it was only theoretical, not probable that counties' populations would shift enough for others to enter or exit the class.

 

661 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bonnewell


1 CA-CR 98-0973, 1 CA-CR 98-0977, 1 CA-CR 98-0978, 1 CA-CR 98-0979, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


196 Ariz. 592; 2 P.3d 682; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 196; 309 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



November 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 7, 1999. Petition for Review DENIED on May 23, 2000 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-99-0566-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County. Cause No. CR 98-0093. The Honorable Howard D. Hinson, Jr., Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), convicting them for setting a leghold trap on public land in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 17-301(D) (formerly § 17-301(D)(1)).


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed their convictions for setting a leghold trap on public land in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 17-301(D) (formerly § 17-301(D)(1)). Defendants argued that the statute was a special or local law in violation of the Arizona Constitution, and that it violated the equal protection clauses of the Arizona and United States constitutions. The court held that the law was not a special law that violated the Arizona Constitution because it rationally furthered a legitimate governmental purpose (to prevent cruelty to animals and injury to others), applied to all persons in Arizona, and benefited no static class of individuals. Thus, the court also held that the statute did not violate the equal protection clauses of either the Arizona or United States Constitutions because it was rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose, and the drafters and voters could have concluded that the statute would achieve that purpose.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions were affirmed because the statute prohibiting leghold traps was not a special law that violated the Arizona Constitution, and because it advanced a legitimate governmental purpose it did not violate the equal protection clauses of either the Arizona or United States constitutions.

Herman v. City of Tucson


2 CA-CV 99-0064


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


197 Ariz. 430; 4 P.3d 973; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 207; 311 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



November 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of Arizona Supreme Court.

DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), ruling in favor of defendant city on cross-motions for summary judgment relating to defense of qualified immunity in negligence action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought a negligence action against defendant city after she was injured while walking toward the band shell area of a park where she was to work for a vendor at a music festival. Defendant asserted qualified immunity under the recreational use statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551. Plaintiff argued the statute did not apply for the following reasons: plaintiff was not a recreational user at the time of her accident; festival was a civic event that did not qualify as a "recreational use"; and the "fee paid" exception to immunity applied because defendant received consideration for plaintiff to be on the premises to sell goods. Defendant argued the permission granted by the premises owner, not the behavior or subjective intentions of each person who enters the land is determinative. The court found that the festival was not a recreational use and plaintiff was not a recreational user within the meaning of § 33-1551.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of defendant vacated and case remanded for further proceedings; plaintiff did not come within the statutory definition of "recreational user" at the time of her accident. Thus, defendant was not entitled to qualified immunity under the statute.

 

663 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Wigglesworth v. Mauldin


1 CA-CV 99-0123


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


195 Ariz. 432; 990 P.2d 26; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 195; 308 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



November 18, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Navajo County. Cause No. CV 98-177. The Honorable Thomas L. Wing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the Superior Court of Navajo County's (Arizona) dismissal of complaint against the governor and deputy warden claiming violation of constitutional rights due to the former governor's decision to not commute appellant's sentences. The court dismissed the complaint for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate appealed from dismissal of complaint against governor and deputy warden, claiming violation of constitutional rights due to the former governor's decision to not commute appellant's sentences; the court dismissed the complaint for failure to state claim upon which relief could be granted. Because appellant had no protected liberty interest in gubernatorial action consistent with the board of executive clemency's recommendation of clemency, the complaint failed to state a violation of an established due process right. Appellant's sentences under a prior sentencing scheme did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. The governor's commutation of sentences of other inmates with similar offenses and similar sentences did not violate appellant's equal protection rights; the governor's discretion to act on the board's recommendations was unfettered. The court did not err in not making findings explaining complaint's deficiencies or in denying appellant leave to amend when appellant did not timely seek leave to amend and lacked a cognizable constitutional claim. The dismissal of appellant's complaint was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of appellant's complaint was affirmed. The complaint failed to state a violation of an established due process right, appellant's sentences did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment, appellant's equal protection rights were not violated, and the court did not err in not making findings explaining complaint's deficiencies or denying appellant leave to amend.

State v. Bonillas


2 CA-CR 99-0137


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


197 Ariz. 96; 3 P.3d 1016; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 194; 308 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



November 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court September 26, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-62248. Honorable Michael Cruikshank, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which granted appellee's motion to suppress cocaine found on appellee, when an officer searched appellee for identification prior to arresting him for failure to provide an operator's license or evidence of identity, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(B).


OVERVIEW: Appellee was arrested for failure to provide an operator's license or evidence of identity, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(B), and was found to possess cocaine when the arresting officer patted him down for identification. Appellee moved the trial court to suppress the cocaine because there was no probable cause to arrest him, and the search was illegal because it occurred before his arrest. The trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress. Appellant state challenged. The court reversed because the officer had probable cause to arrest appellee for violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(B) when he did not produce his driver's license, and the search for identification was permissible, even though it occurred before the arrest, because the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant at the time he initiated the search.


OUTCOME: Grant of motion to suppress reversed because the arresting officer had probable cause to arrest appellee when he did not produce his driver's license, and the officer's search for identification was permissible before the arrest because the officer had probable cause to arrest appellee when he initiated the search.

Stulce v. Salt River Project Agric. Improvement & Power Dist.


1 CA-CV 99-0024


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed dismissal of their complaint based on failure to bring suit against a public entity within one year pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-821 entered by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) in a case where plaintiffs sustained serious personal injuries while doing electrical work.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sustained injuries on March 16, 1997. Their complaint alleged defendant government corporation negligently turned on an electric current, causing serious injury. Within 180 days of injury, plaintiffs filed a notice of claim with defendant, as required by Arizona law. Defendant denied the claim by not responding by July 16, 1997, within 60 days after the claim notice was filed. Plaintiffs believed they had one year from the time of the claim notice denial in which to sue. They filed suit on July 8, 1998. Defendant moved to dismiss. It alleged the claim had to filed by March 16, 1998. The trial court agreed with defendant. Plaintiffs appealed. The court held relevant statutory provisions did not allow plaintiffs to use the notice of claim to toll the one-year filing requirement in actions against a public entity since statute required cause of action itself to be filed within one-year of injury.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order of dismissal affirmed because plaintiffs were aware of the claim they had against defendant government corporation, yet they failed to file their cause of action in a timely manner as required by Arizona statutory law.

State v. Taylor


2 CA-CR 98-0451


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


196 Ariz. 584; 2 P.3d 674; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 186; 306 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



October 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] State of Arizona's Petition for Review Denied by Supreme Court May 23, 2000 CR-99-0511-PR. Appellant's Cross-Petition for Review Denied.
A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court June 23, 2000.
Subsequent civil proceeding at In re Commitment of Olin Gene Taylor, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 183 (Ariz. Ct. App., Nov. 10, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-60293. Honorable Deborah Ward, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of child molestation from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona)on constitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of child molestation contending that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4511, allowing the admission of a minor's prior recorded statement, was unconstitutional and also that the admission of the victim's statement to her stepmother as an excited utterance was error. The court reversed holding that Ariz. Rev. Code § 13-451 was an unconstitutional exercise of legislative power because it expanded on, conflicted with, and engulfed the court's rules. Neither was the statement admissible under Ariz. R. Evid. 803(24)'s catchall exception to the hearsay rule because it was not more probative than the victim's in-court testimony, both being similar. Such bolstering was impermissible. The admission was prejudicial error when the jury's verdict may have been affected. The victim's statement to her stepmother, however, was properly admitted as an excited utterance because the statement was made while the victim was still under the stress of the incident.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was reversed because statute allowing admission of minor victim's prior recorded statement was an unconstitutional exercise of legislative power, statement not admissible under another hearsay exception, and its admission may have affected verdict; however, victim's statement to her stepmother was admissible under the excited utterance exception.

669 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vera


2 CA-CR 98-0350


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


196 Ariz. 342; 996 P.2d 1246; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 201; 309 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



September 21, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review - DENIED by Arizona Supreme Court. Redesignated as Opinion November 24, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-59480. Honorable Deborah Ward, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Pima County (Arizona), suppressing evidence against appellee and dismissing criminal charges against him based upon alleged violations of U.S. Const. amend. IV and XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellee's automobile was stopped by police because it had a cracked windshield. As a result of evidence seized during the stop, appellee was indicted on felony charges. Appellee's motion to suppress the evidence was granted on the basis that the automobile stop and subsequent search were in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV and XIV. The charges against appellee were dismissed. The appellate court ruled that the traffic stop to investigate possible vehicle equipment violation was constitutional, and that the decision to stop appellee's automobile was reasonable because the police had probable cause to believe that a traffic violation occurred. Further, the court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-957.01(A) required a vehicle to have an adequate windshield, and that whether the windshield on an automobile was adequate was first investigated by a police officer and next determined by a fact finder if the officer issued a traffic citation for an alleged violation. The court reversed the trial court's judgment, concluding that the officer was not required to determine the adequacy of the windshield before he stopped appellee's automobile to investigate the obviously cracked windshield.


OUTCOME: Judgment granting appellee's motion to suppress and dismissing charges against appellee was reversed where the decision to stop an automobile was reasonable; the police had probable cause to believe that a traffic violation occurred, it was undisputed that appellee's windshield was cracked, and the officer thus had a legitimate reason to stop appellee's vehicle to investigate the adequacy of his windshield.

 

670 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Kessen v. Stewart


1 CA-IC 98-0040


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


195 Ariz. 488; 990 P.2d 689; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 149; 302 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



August 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Name of this Case has been Amended by Order September 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action -- Industrial Commission. ICA Claim No.: 93232 - 380645. Carrier No.: None. Administrative Law Judge Gay Conrad Kruglick.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought review of a Special Action proceeding of the Industrial Commission of Arizona (ICA), in which ICA commuted respondent employee's award of unscheduled permanent partial disability benefits to a lump sum.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners challenged the Industrial Commission of Arizona's (ICA) commutation of respondent employees workers' compensation award to a lump sum without first obtaining their consent, allegedly required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1067(B).The court held that the ICA was not required to obtain a private, uninsured employer's consent before commuting a workers' compensation award to a lump sum. These employers were not "carriers" by statutory definition. The court examined the large scheme of the Arizona workers' compensation statutes and found that the disparate treatment was justified because uninsured employers were not in compliance with the workers' compensation statutes and, thus, not entitled to their protections and benefits. Therefore, a rational basis for the disparate treatment existed, enabling the legislation to survive an equal protection challenge. The court dismissed petitioners' due process argument because petitioners received notice and an opportunity for a hearing on the lump-sum commutation, which their attorney waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commutation of the workers' compensation award to a lump-sum payment. Uninsured employers were not "carriers" under the applicable statute; therefore, the Industrial Commission of Arizona did not have to obtain petitioners' consent before commuting the award.

 

671 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Brandon H.


1 CA-JV 98-0225


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


195 Ariz. 387; 988 P.2d 619; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 133; 300 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



July 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on October 26, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-99-0337-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. JV-142750. The Honorable Kristin C. Hoffman, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona). Pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-3320(A)(3), the trial court suspended defendant's driving privileges until the age of 18 after defendant pled delinquent to a charge of criminal damage.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile pled delinquent to criminal damage in exchange for a promise by the state to dismiss other charges for unlawful use of a vehicle and curfew violation. As part of the plea agreement, defendant's driving privileges were suspended pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-3320(A)(3). Defendant was placed on probation and required to perform community service. On appeal, defendant argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-3320(A)(3), which suspended the driving privileges of juveniles who had been convicted of criminal damage, violated the equal protection and due process clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court rejected defendant's argument and affirmed the trial court's decision. Arizona Rev. Stat. § 28-3320(A)(3) did not violate either the equal protection clause or the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The statute was not arbitrary and was reasonably related to the legitimate state interest of deterring juveniles from committing crimes. The statute did not distinguish between juveniles based on age and imposed the same punishment on all juveniles who committed criminal damage. The statute was also subject to procedural safeguards.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that suspended defendant juvenile's driving privileges until the age of eighteen after defendant pled delinquent to a charge of criminal damage. The statute did not violate either the equal protection clause or the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The statute was reasonably related to a legitimate state interest because loss of driving privileges could give juveniles an incentive to renounce crime.

 

672 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Arizona Bd. of Regents


1 CA-CV 98-0627


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


195 Ariz. 214; 986 P.2d 247; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 125; 299 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 46



July 8, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 97-92076. The Honorable Linda K. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant student appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County, which held that appellee university was not liable in tort for appellant's injuries stemming from an accident appellant suffered while attending a university function.


OVERVIEW: Appellant student was injured while attending a fair held on appellee university grounds. Appellant sued appellee in tort for injuries he sustained from jumping on a trampoline machine set up at the fair. Appellant claimed that appellee university and appellee contractor failed to adequately maintain the trampoline, warn users of its known dangers, and properly service its use. He also claimed that appellee university was liable for permitting the inherently dangerous activity and for negligently supervising the activities of the other appellees. The trial court granted appellee university's motion for summary judgment on the basis that it was immune from suit under a state recreational use statute. On appeal the court held that the recreational use statute did not apply because appellant was not claiming premises liability but instead was claiming that the university permitted an inherently dangerous activity and negligently supervised the parties responsible for the activity. Further, the court held that appellant was not a recreational user as contemplated by the statute. The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: Appellant student prevailed on appeal and the court reversed judgment in favor of appellee university, holding that appellee university could be held liable in tort for injuries appellant student sustained while jumping on a trampoline set upon university grounds. The court further held that the state recreational use statute did not provide the university with immunity from tort based on these facts.

PLM Tax Certificate Program 1991-92, LP v. Denton Invs., Inc.


1 CA-CV 98-0666


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


195 Ariz. 210; 986 P.2d 243; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 122; 299 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 50



July 6, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at PLM Tax Certificate Program 1991-92, L.P. v. Schweikert, 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 130 (Ariz. Ct. App., July 17, 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of summary judgment from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which allowed appellees to foreclose tax liens on two lots appellant acquired from the Resolution Trust Corporation.


OVERVIEW: Appellees purchased tax liens on a lot which was in Resolution Trust Corporation (RTC) receivership. The lot was sold by RTC to appellant. Under the Financial Institution Reform, Recovery, and Enforcement Act, 12 U.S.C.S. § 1825, states and local government were prevented from imposing taxes on property held by the RTC as receiver, and no property of the RTC was subject to levy, attachment, garnishment, foreclosure, or sale without the consent of RTC, nor could any involuntary lien attach to the property of the RTC. Therefore, the tax lien on the lot in RTC receivership and, thus, the purchase of that lien by appellees was invalid. Appellant redeemed the taxes on a second lot, and attorney fees were granted to appellee in the full amount incurred in the purchase of tax liens on both lots. The appellate court found no reasonable basis for the awarding of fees incurred for the lot that was sold in error to appellee. Determination of reasonable fees in regard to the redemption of the lot was to be determined on remand.


OUTCOME: Judgment for appellee allowing foreclosure on tax liens was reversed and the case was remanded, where the lien on one property was not valid since it did not attach until after the lot was in Resolution Trust Corporation receivership; attorney fees assessed on both lots was unreasonable because the fees were assessed after appellant redeemed taxes on the second lot.

State v. Heinze


1 CA-CV 92-0410


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


196 Ariz. 126; 993 P.2d 1090; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 116; 298 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



June 29, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended By Order, Filed July 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 91-17871. The Honorable Stanley F. Goodfarb, Judge (Retired).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) awarding a declaratory judgment to appellees, victims and tortfeasor, mandating that appellant indemnify appellee tortfeasor in the sexual harassment suit brought by appellee victims.


OVERVIEW: Appellee tortfeasor, a state employee, was sued by appellee victims for sexual harassment and misconduct in the form of offensive remarks, quid pro quo sexual demands, and rape. Appellees, victims and tortfeasor, sought and received a declaratory judgment mandating that appellant state indemnify the tortfeasor because of actions taken while acting within the scope of his authorization. Appellant state argued that the record did not support a grant of summary judgment or a declaratory decision that appellee tortfeasor acted within the scope of his employment or authorization. The court agreed, noting that the inference should have been made by a trier of fact, not on a summary motion. The court therefore reversed the granting of appellees' declaratory judgment on that issue. However, the court held that it was not violative of public policy to provide a fund of insurance to compensate people injured by government agents while acting in their governmental capacities. The court additionally found that a trier of fact should have decided whether the felony exclusion law was applicable to the case. The court therefore reversed and remanded on the indemnity issue.


OUTCOME: The awarding of a declaratory judgment to appellees, victims and tortfeasor, was reversed because the court held that the issue of whether indemnity was mandated was better left to a jury and should not have been decided on a summary motion.

Aranda v. Industrial Comm'n


1 CA-IC 98-0113


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


195 Ariz. 403; 989 P.2d 157; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 112; 298 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 55



June 24, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review GRANTED October 28, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-99-0303-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action--Industrial Commission. Claim No. 93147-331814. Carrier No. 93-20513. Administrative Law Judge Joann C. Gaffaney.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision by the Arizona Industrial Commission that suspended his disability payments during the period of his incarceration pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1031.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the administrative law judge's finding that petitioner's disability payments were suspended pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1031 while he was incarcerated. The court found that § 23-1031 was not unlawfully retroactive because it did not change the status of petitioner's benefits. The court held that no substantive due process rights were violated because even though workers' compensation payments were considered property, they were statutory rights and not fundamental or substantive rights. The court held that the disparate treatment of prisoners and non-prisoners was founded on real differences rationally related to the purposes of workers' compensation and was therefore proper. The court noted that injured workers were compensated for their lost earning capacity, but an incarcerated person was removed from the labor market, and his payments would resume once when he returned. The court noted petitioner was given notice and opportunity to be heard before his suspension of payments occurred, and it dismissed petitioner's remaining contentions.


OUTCOME: Judgment suspending petitioner's permanent disability payments while he was incarcerated was affirmed. The statute was not unlawfully retroactive because it did not change the status of petitioner's benefits. The court found no due process rights violated because petitioner's rights were not fundamental and the disparate treatment of prisoners and non-prisoners was founded on differences rationally related to workers' compensation.

Dickey v. City of Flagstaff


1 CA-CV 98-0026


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


197 Ariz. 422; 4 P.3d 965; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 95; 296 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



May 27, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Dickey v. City of Flagstaff, 2001 Ariz. LEXIS 32 (Ariz., Feb. 23, 2001)
Vacated by Dickey v. City of Flagstaff, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 34 (Ariz., Apr. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Coconino County. Cause No. CV 95-0564. The Honorable J. Michael Flournoy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, minor child, mother, and guardian ad litem of child, challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona) granting summary judgment to appellee city in appellants' action for negligence in the minor child's sledding accident on defendant's property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor child was injured when he went sledding on appellee city's property. Appellants, mother and guardian ad litem, sued appellee cite, alleging it was negligent in that it did not make safe the areas in which children sledded and did not attempt to prevent sledding. Appellants also alleged that the attractive nuisance doctrine applied. Appellee's motion for summary judgment was granted after appellee argued the Recreational Use Statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551, gave appellee immunity and that the attractive nuisance doctrine did not apply. On appeal, the court held that appellee did not engage in any conduct rising to the level of gross negligence and that the Recreational Use Statute applied. The court noted that appellee attempted to discourage sledding on its property but that the signs kept being torn down and used for sleds. The court also noted that appellee did not make the sledding area an artificial condition by removing shrubs and bushes. The court found that appellant minor child was supervised by his stepmother, and thus the attractive nuisance doctrine did not apply. Therefore, summary judgment in favor of appellee city was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The award of summary judgment to appellee city was affirmed because there was no evidence to support a finding that it was grossly negligent in allowing people to sled on its property. Additionally, the fact that appellant minor child was supervised by an adult negated the application of the attractive nuisance doctrine.

U S W. Communs. v. Ariz. Corp. Comm'n


1 CA-CV 97-0517


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


197 Ariz. 16; 3 P.3d 936; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 86; 295 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



May 18, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CV 95-14284, 96-03355, 96-03356, 96-08891. The Honorable Steven D. Sheldon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telephone company sought review of an order of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which denied its motion for partial summary judgment and granted appellee agency's cross-motion for summary judgment in a suit challenging appellee's rules to allow companies to compete with appellant for customers.


OVERVIEW: Appellee agency promulgated rules allowing companies to compete with appellant telephone company. Appellant filed suit asserting breach of contract and asserting the rules were invalid. Appellant sought review of the order denying its motion but granting appellee's motion for summary judgment. The court held appellant's claims were ripe; appellant did not have to exhaust administrative avenues before pursuing its breach of contract action and properly exhausted such remedies in its challenge to the rules. The court found appellant did not have a breach of contract claim because no contract was created by the state constitution or statutes. Certain rules were properly promulgated because they were related to appellee's plenary power and did not have to be reviewed by the attorney general under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1044. The rules relating to the issuance of competitive licenses required such review as they were not related to ratemaking and not within appellee's plenary power. The court affirmed the dismissal of the breach of contract claim and agreed certain rules did not require attorney general review, but it reversed as to the remainder of the rules which required review.


OUTCOME: Order denying appellant telephone company's motion for summary judgment and granting appellee agency's motion was affirmed in part because appellant failed to establish contract existed and, thus, failed to state a claim for breach of contract; order was reversed in part because certain of the challenged rules were not related to ratemaking, were not within appellee's plenary power, and were, thus, invalid until reviewed by the attorney general.

Martin v. Reinstein


1 CA-SA 98-0260


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


195 Ariz. 293; 987 P.2d 779; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 83; 295 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



May 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED October 28, 1999, Supreme Court No. CV-99-0247-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CV 15634, CV 97-16011, CV 97-16640, CV 97-17349, CV 97-17856, CV 97-19181, CV 98-06110, CV 97-22868, CV 98-00471, CV 98-12186, CV 98-10927, CV 98-07654, and CV 98-15652. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), in their special action challenging the constitutionality of the state's Sexually Violent Persons Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 36-3701-3716.


OVERVIEW: The Sexually Violent Persons Act (Act), Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 36-3701-3716, allowed the state to confine persons who were previously found guilty of violent sexual acts or were charged with such crimes but were deemed incompetent to stand trial for them, if those persons also suffered from a mental disorder that made them likely to engage in acts of sexual violence in the future. Petitioners, persons against whom sexually violent person petitions were filed, brought a special action petition challenging the constitutionality of the Act. The court ruled that the Act was civil in nature because it focused on treatment for sexually violent persons and protection of the public. Further, the court held that the Act did not violate constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws and double jeopardy because it was civil, not penal. Also, the court found that the Act rationally advanced legitimate governmental goals, namely, protecting citizens from individuals who were judicially determined to be dangerous and treating sexually violent persons. The court denied the special petition, concluding that reasonable classification did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: Special petition challenging the constitutionality of the Sexually Violent Persons Act was denied where the statute was civil in nature and the statute rationally advanced the state's legitimate governmental goals of protecting its citizens from individuals who were judicially determined to be dangerous and of treating sexually violent persons.

Rodriguez v. Arellano


1 CA-SA 99-0051


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


194 Ariz. 211; 979 P.2d 539; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 84; 295 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



May 13, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 98-15401. The Honorable Silvia Arellano, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Finding that defendant could not sustain his burden of going forward under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 16.2(b), by proving that police seized the evidence against defendant during a warrantless search, the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) struck defendant's motion to suppress with leave to refile. Defendant filed a special action to determine whether a defendant may satisfy the initial burden of going forward by proving the lack of a warrant.


OVERVIEW: After the prosecution filed an information charging various drug offenses, defendant moved to suppress evidence seized as the result of an allegedly illegal search. Defendant showed the uncontested fact that police conducted a warrantless search to seize the evidence. The trial court denied defendant's motion, concluding that defendant did not carry the burden of going forward under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 16.2(b). Defendant sought review by filing a special action. Finding that defendant lacked an adequate remedy by appeal, the court asserted special action jurisdiction to review the trial court's denial of the motion to suppress the fruits of an allegedly illegal search. Under Rule 16.2(b), the court held that defendant satisfied the initial burden of going forward by proving the lack of a warrant. Because the challenged evidence was obtained without a warrant, the prosecution had to carry the entire evidentiary burden pursuant to the "warrant/no warrant" dichotomy recognized by federal and a majority of state courts. Therefore, the court vacated and remanded the trial court's order that granted the prosecution's motion to strike defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: Accepting jurisdiction of defendant's special action, the court vacated and remanded the trial court's order granting the prosecution's motion to strike defendant's motion to suppress evidence. By proving the lack of a warrant, defendant carried the initial burden of going forward. Therefore, the prosecution had to carry the burden of persuading the trial court that the search and seizure fell under a valid exception to the warrant requirement.

Comeau v. Arizona State Bd. of Dental Exam'rs


1 CA-CV 98-0344


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


196 Ariz. 102; 993 P.2d 1066; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 81; 295 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



May 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on February 8, 2000 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-99-0256-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 96-20894. The Honorable Steven D. Sheldon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dentist sought review of an order from the Superior Court in Maricopa (Arizona), which affirmed appellee agency's censure of appellant after an investigative interview.


OVERVIEW: Appellee agency conducted an investigative interview of appellant dentist and censured him after finding he engaged in unprofessional conduct with respect to fitting a patient with dentures. The finding of misconduct and the censure were affirmed on appeal, and appellant sought further review. The court held the investigative interview did not violate appellant's procedural due process rights. Appellant was afforded the opportunity to be heard, had sufficient notice of the charges and evidence against him, presented a defense, testified, and was represented by counsel. The court found that although notice of the investigative interview was insufficient because it did not apprise appellant of his right to a formal hearing, the deficiency was harmless because appellant and his counsel were aware of such right. Substantial evidence supported appellee's decision and its sanction was not arbitrary, capricious, or an abuse of discretion. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 32-1263.02, allowing appellee to impose sanctions after a hearing, was constitutional because the hearing qualified as a due process hearing. The court, thus, upheld the order affirming appellee's decision.


OUTCOME: Order affirming appellee agency's finding that appellant dentist committed professional misconduct and censuring him was upheld because appellant's procedural due process rights were not violated; appellant was afforded the opportunity to be heard and was sufficiently notified of the charges against him. Substantial evidence supported appellee's findings, and the sanction imposed was not an abuse of discretion.

In re Kory L.


1 CA-JV 98-0199


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


194 Ariz. 215; 979 P.2d 543; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 82; 295 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



May 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended By Order Filed May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV-131675. The Honorable Jesse B. Filkins, Jr., Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the order from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which held that appellant was bound by juvenile's stipulation, in a delinquency proceeding plea agreement, regarding the amount of restitution due.


OVERVIEW: Juvenile pleaded delinquent to criminal trespass and stipulated to a restitution amount. After appellant mother was informed that she could be held responsible for the restitution, a restitution hearing was requested. At the hearing, the court held that, based on Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-341(H), appellant was bound by juvenile's stipulation. On appeal, appellee state argued that appellant lacked standing to appeal because appellant was not a party to the delinquency proceeding. The appellate court held that failing to appoint counsel for appellant during the delinquency proceeding was not erroneous because appellant did not have a right to counsel under Ariz. R. P. Juv. Ct. 6, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-225. Furthermore, appellant had no due process right to counsel during the delinquency proceeding. In addition, the appellate court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-341(H) was constitutional because it consistent with established public policy that parents were financially responsible for their children's actions. However, the appellate court remanded the case, holding that appellant was denied due process to a meaningful hearing before the Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-341(H) restitution order.


OUTCOME: The appellate court remanded appellant mother's case regarding an order that held appellant responsible for juvenile's stipulated restitution in a juvenile proceeding. The appellate court directed allowance for appellant to have a meaningful restitution hearing or allowance for waiver of the right because appellant was denied due process to a meaningful hearing before the restitution order was entered.

3613 Ltd. v. Department of Liquor Licenses & Control


1 CA-CV 98-0035


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


194 Ariz. 178; 978 P.2d 1282; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 61; 293 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



April 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 96-12896. The Honorable Roger W. Kaufman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a business operating a topless bar and its owner, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) affirming a decision of the Department of Liquor that suspended their liquor license unless the controlling person ceased her business association with a convicted felon, raising a number of constitutional challenges to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4-210(A)(12), the applicable statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a business operating a topless bar and its owner, sought review of a trial court decision affirming a decision of the Department of Liquor that suspended their liquor license unless the controlling person ceased her business association with a convicted felon. The court rejected appellants' constitutional challenges to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4-210(A)(12), the applicable statute, and affirmed the lower court decision. The court held that the standards set forth in the statute were sufficiently clear and limited to guide the department in carrying out the purposes of the legislation, even though the terms "associates with" and "association" were not defined in the statute; and that the department was not constitutionally required to promulgate its own rules. The court also rejected appellants' challenges based on U.S. Const. amend. I, holding that the maintenance of a liquor license was not a mode of expression protected from prior restraint. Although appellants' right to free association might have been curtailed by the statute, the right was not absolute, and the state had a significant interest in regulating commercial activity in the liquor industry.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court, holding that the statutory standards were sufficiently clear to guide the department and that the department was not required to promulgate its own rules; that maintenance of a liquor license was not protected by the First Amendment from prior restraints; and that although appellants' free association rights might have been curtailed, the state had a significant interest in regulating the liquor industry.
