Badia v. City of Casa Grande


2 CA-CV 98-0122


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


195 Ariz. 349; 988 P.2d 134; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 40; 291 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



March 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court November 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 319337. Honorable Robert Donfeld, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, individually and on behalf of the estate and children of her deceased daughter, appealed from a summary judgment granted in favor of defendants, a political subdivision and two couples, in the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), after a change in venue occurred, contending that while in police custody she had suffered excessive force and due process violation under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and that officers had been grossly negligent.


OVERVIEW: Decedent was murdered by her boyfriend after being released from police custody. Plaintiff, individually and on behalf of the estate and children of her daughter, the decedent, filed suit against defendants, a political subdivision, police officers, and their spouses, for all but one defendant. After a venue change, defendants filed a summary judgment motion that was granted by the trial court. Plaintiff appealed, contending that in police custody the decedent had suffered excessive force and deprivation of due process in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and gross negligance by defendants officers. The court examined plaintiff's allegations and stated that § 1983 due process did not require defendants to protect decedent after her release from their custody and that there was no constitutional duty to protect decedent upon release. Also, a reasonable trier of fact could not find that defendants' alleged acts or omissions proximately caused decedent's death after her release from custody, nor that defendants had evil motive or callous indifference to decedent's federally protected rights. The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment to defendants on all claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendants on all claims because a reasonable trier of fact could not find that defendants' alleged acts or omissions proximately caused decedent's death and that those involved had evil motive or callous indifference to decedent's federally protected rights. The court stated that defendants had no constitutional duty to protect decedent after her release from custody.

Goodman v. Samaritan Health Sys.


1 CA-CV 97-0392


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


195 Ariz. 502; 990 P.2d 1061; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 36; 291 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



March 16, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED November 30, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-99-0157-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 94-07672. The Honorable Linda A. Akers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician appealed from a grant of summary judgment to defendant hospital in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), contending that defendant was not statutorily immune from his allegations of negligent peer review and malicious prosecution. Several hospitals and the state hospital association filed an amici curiae brief in favor of the summary judgment to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff physician filed a complaint against defendant hospital in the trial court alleging claims of negligent peer review and malicious prosecution and seeking damages consisting of attorneys' fees, expert witness fees, pain and suffering, and punitive damages. Defendant filed a motion for summary judgment asserting that it was entitled to complete immunity pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 36-445.02(B). The trial court granted judgment for defendant on its immunity defense and dismissed plaintiff's claims. Plaintiff appealed, contending that the absolute immunity granted by statute to peer review participants violated the anti-abrogation, due process, and privileges or immunities clauses of the Arizona Constitution. The court found that the anti-abrogation clause, Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6, could be circumscribed by a legislative statute that denied or limited damages for a certain violation and that the state had a compelling reason to grant immunity to medical peer reviewers in § 36-445.02(B) as such reviews furthered a legitimate state interest in improving hospital care and preventing deaths. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendant hospital because upon application of a rational basis test, the court found that a state law granting statutory immunity from suits seeking money damages to medical professionals involved in peer review served a legitimate state interest in improving patient care and reducing hospital deaths.

Pavlik v. Chinle Unified Sch. Dist. No. 24


1 CA-CV 98-0203


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


195 Ariz. 148; 985 P.2d 633; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 31; 290 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 42



March 11, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on September 21, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-99-0149-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Apache County. Cause No. CV 96-037. The Honorable Michael C. Nelson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant-appellant school district challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Apache County (Arizona), which voided defendant-appellant's termination of plaintiff-appellee high school teacher, who had been placed on administrative leave with pay because of allegations that he had behaved inappropriately toward some female students.


OVERVIEW: Defendant-appellant school district challenged a trial court decision reinstating plaintiff -appellee teacher, who was terminated by defendant-appellant's board after being placed on administrative leave with pay after allegations that he had behaved inappropriately toward some female students. The court applied the standard that a party asserting bias had the burden of rebutting the presumption of fairness and establishing a disqualifying interest, and found that plaintiff-appellee had not met his burden of proving either personal bias or institutional bias by board members. The court also held that the record lacked evidence to rebut the presumption that the board was fair and impartial. The court also found that plaintiff-appellee's pre-termination suspension was constitutionally permissible since it was with pay, and that some procedural irregularities did not prejudice plaintiff-appellee. Concluding that the trial court had abused its discretion, the court reversed the decision for plaintiff-appellee and remanded with instructions to reinstate defendant-appellant's decision to terminate plaintiff-appellee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case back to the trial court, with instructions to reinstate the decision of defendant-appellant school district's board. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion in concluding that plaintiff-appellee's due process rights were violated and that being placed on paid administrative leave without first being provided a copy of the charges against him prejudiced his ability to present his case.

 

687 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


City of Tucson v. Whiteco Metrocom


2 CA-CV 98-0064


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


194 Ariz. 390; 983 P.2d 759; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 69; 293 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



February 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Redesignated as Opinion April 14, 1999.
A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court October 26, 1999.
A Cross-Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court October 26, 1999.
Related proceeding at City of Tucson v. Clear Channel Outdoor, Inc., 206 Ariz. 335, 78 P.3d 1056, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 179 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 301491. Honorable Kenneth Lee, Judge. Honorable J. Richard Hannah, Judge.
Outdoor Sys., Inc. v. City of Mesa, 997 F.2d 604, 1993 U.S. App. LEXIS 15898 (9th Cir. Ariz., 1993)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order of the Arizona Supreme Court, which denied its petition for review, and appellee company similarly appealed from a denial of its cross-petition for review in a case in which the trial court determined that the city's "vacant lot" ordinance was unenforceable against appellee/cross-appellant, and that four of its billboards were not subject to removal.


OVERVIEW: In an action for equitable relief, appellant city sued appellee company seeking the removal of several billboards, claiming the billboards violated the city's vacant lot ordinance. The city also claimed some of the billboards were changed and had lost the protection of the nonconforming use statute. The trial court granted appellee's motion for partial summary judgment. After a bench trial, the court permitted appellee to retain three billboards, ordered appellee to remove the second advertising face from another billboard, and ordered appellee to remove 11 of the contested billboards. On appeal, the court determined that partial summary judgment in favor of appellee was proper on the vacant lot ordinance issue, and that the city's cause of action was not a vested right. The court also held that the court did not abuse its discretion in ordering appellee to remove only the second billboard face. The court, however, could not uphold the trial court's judgment that the city should have been estopped from asserting that the permits for three of the billboards were issued in violation of zoning regulations.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order permitting appellee to retain three billboards and order to remove a second face from another billboard was affirmed, but the trial court's order to remove contested billboards was vacated and remanded because the city should have been estopped from asserting that permits for those billboards were issued in violation of then existing zoning regulations.

 

688 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Grosvenor Holdings L.C. v. City of Peoria


1 CA-CV 98-0472


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


195 Ariz. 137; 985 P.2d 622; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 15; 287 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 64



January 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on September 21, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-99-0061-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 98-07842. The Honorable John R. Sticht, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city, city council, and citizens' group sought review of a decision in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment to appellee developer on its claim that a referendum petition filed by appellant citizen's group was untimely.


OVERVIEW: The lower court found that the vote by appellant city council officials to approve a rezoning request by appellee developer, rather than the adoption of the rezoning ordinance, was the referable legislative act. Therefore, the lower court held that the referendum petition filed by appellant citizens' group was untimely because it was filed more than 30 days after the minutes recording the vote were approved. The court affirmed because the lower court had properly applied the bright line rule, and, in cases challenging compliance with constitutional and statutory requirements, strict compliance was required. Attaching the approved minutes to the referendum petitions was sufficient without the attachment of appellee's stipulations of development conditions because to require otherwise would improperly amplify the scope of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 19-121(E). The court rejected appellants' waiver and laches argument although suit had been filed more than a year after verification of the petition signatures. The complaint had been filed well before the scheduled election and appellant citizen's group had ample time to mount a defense and present their case.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court holding a referendum petition on appellee developer's rezoning request untimely filed was affirmed because the bright line rule required the petition to be filed within 30 days of the approval of the minutes recording the rezoning decision, rather than within 30 days of the adoption of the rezoning ordinance, as appellant citizens' group had done.

Graville v. Dodge (In re Graville)


1 CA-CV 98-0104, 1 CA-CV 98-0150, (CONSOLIDATED)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


195 Ariz. 119; 985 P.2d 604; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 16; 287 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 68



January 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on September 21, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-99-0091-PR.
The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court December 20, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. DR 97-90192. The Honorable James H. Keppel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a judgment from the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) that awarded appellee maternal grandparents visitation with the children of their deceased daughter.


OVERVIEW: The trial court awarded appellee maternal grandparents visitation with the children of their deceased daughter. On review, appellant, the children's father, challenged the constitutionality of the grandparent visitation statute. He also argued that the amount of visitation awarded was excessive. The trial court granted appellees visitation with their granddaughters for four to eight hours twice a month, two days during Christmas break, and a three-day weekend during the summer. On appeal, the court noted that although a parent's right to custody and control was constitutionally protected, it was not beyond regulation. Under their constitutional powers, states may regulate the well-being of children. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-409 was rationally related to furthering the state's legitimate interest in enabling children to become responsible adults by fostering relationships between grandchildren and their grandparents. The court also found that the visitation awarded was reasonable and did not constitute an abuse of discretion. The children had spent extended periods of their young lives living in the grandparents' home.


OUTCOME: The trial court's award of visitation rights to appellee grandparents was affirmed because the grandparent visitation statute at issue was constitutional and because the time allotted to appellees for visitation with the children was reasonable.

Bills v. Arizona Prop. & Cas. Ins. Guar. Fund


2 CA-CV 98-0130


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


194 Ariz. 488; 984 P.2d 574; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 18; 288 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



January 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Filed and Granted. Dismissed by Order of Arizona Supreme Court January 28, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 311771. Honorable Michael Alfred, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action alleging negligence, breach of contract, and bad faith, plaintiff appealed the grant of partial summary judgment to defendant, a state insurance fund, by the Pima County Superior Court (Arizona).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff appealed from the trial court's entry of partial summary judgment for defendant. In an underlying wrongful death action arising from a motor vehicle accident in which her husband was killed, plaintiff alleged "dram shop" liability against a company. The company became insolvent and was placed into receivership. Defendant fund then assumed all outstanding covered claims. Defendant refused to settle the claim and a jury verdict was entered for plaintiff. Later plaintiff filed suit against defendant alleging negligence, breach of contract, and bad faith. The trial court entered partial summary judgment as to plaintiff's causes of action sounding in tort. The court found that defendant fund was not subject to common law tort claims in connection with its handling of covered claims. The court noted that it must construe provisions together, in the context of the overall statutory scheme, and aim to achieve consistency among them. The court found that defendant was not subject to common law tort claims in connection with its handling of covered claims because neither defendant fund nor its agents routinely engaged in bad faith practices in handling covered claims.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of partial summary judgment to defendant state insurance fund was affirmed because the fund was not subject to liability on plaintiff's tort claims. Defendant fund did not routinely engage in bad faith practices when handling covered claims.

Airport Props. v. Maricopa County


1 CA-CV 97-0597


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


195 Ariz. 89; 985 P.2d 574; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 9; 287 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



January 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on September 21, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-99-0121-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CV 95-00449 and CV 95-18145. The Honorable William P. Sargeant, III, Judge. The Honorable Silvia R. Arellano, Judge. The Honorable Brian R. Hauser, Judge. The Honorable Anna M. Baca, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed an order of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) that granted summary judgment for plaintiffs in an action challenging defendant's right to assess ad valorem property taxes after the repeal of Arizona's possessory interest taxing scheme.


OVERVIEW: Defendant county appealed from summary judgment for plaintiffs, which challenged defendant's right to tax plaintiffs' interests in an airport as real property and to assess ad valorem property taxes against those interests after the repeal of Arizona's possessory interest taxing scheme. The trial court found that plaintiffs' airport improvements interests were no longer subject to ad valorem property taxes because the repeal removed the required statutory mechanism for taxing possessory interests and showed the legislature's intent that such interests not be taxed. On review the appellate court noted that the best indicator of the drafters' intent was a provision's language. The judgment was affirmed on appeal because a legislative decision not to provide for ad valorem taxation of possessory interests did not "exempt" them from taxation. Possessory interests were a discrete category of property. The legislative decision did not "exempt" them. It omitted them from the state's exercise of its power to tax by dint of sovereign political discretion. Nothing in the ad valorem property taxation scheme suggested a legislative intent that possessory interests be taxed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of summary judgment to plaintiffs was affirmed because defendant county was unable to assess any ad valorem property taxes against plaintiffs' interests after the repeal of the possessory interest taxing scheme.

 

692 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


1 CA-CR 97-0673


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


196 Ariz. 530; 2 P.3d 89; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 11; 287 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



January 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on May 23, 2000 by Arizona Supreme Court CR 99-0055-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR 96-12400. The Honorable Alfred J. Rogers, Judge, and The Honorable Michael A. Yarnell, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of January 19, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 4.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) his conviction and sentence for attempted first-degree murder and aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his convictions for attempted first-degree murder and aggravated assault. Counsel for defendant filed a brief stating that he has searched the record and found no arguable question of law upon which an appeal could be based. The court noted that in Arizona counsel submits the brief to the court and the defendant. The defendant is then given the opportunity to file a brief. After receiving all briefing, the court reviews the entire record for reversible error. If any arguable issue presents itself, the court directs appointed counsel to brief the issue. Only after the court has ascertained that counsel has conscientiously performed his or her duty to review the record, and has itself reviewed the record for reversible error and found none, will the court allow counsel to withdraw. The court found that the procedure permitted counsel to perform ethically, while simultaneously ensuring that an indigent defendant's constitutional rights to due process, equal protection, and effective assistance of counsel were protected. Defendant's convictions were affirmed because there was no reversible error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for attempted first-degree murder and aggravated assault was affirmed because there was no reversible error found in the record. Defendant's counsel was permitted to withdraw due to the lack of any arguable question of law upon which an appeal could be based.

 

693 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Cuvelier v. Schmitz


2 CA-CV 98-0223


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


193 Ariz. 479; 974 P.2d 995; 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 1; 287 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



January 7, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court April 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 328724. Honorable Michael J. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which determined that a municipal initiative petition, circulated by appellee, should have been placed on the next statewide general election ballot.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, who helped circulate a municipal initiative petition, filed a special action complaint seeking an order to compel appellant town to place the initiative on the next statewide general election ballot. The trial court determined that the petition should have been placed on the ballot. Because it was impossible to place the initiative on the ballot at that time, the trial court ordered appellant to call a special election. Appellant sought review, and the court reversed the judgment. In order to render appellant's initiative procedure as nearly as practicable the same as those in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 19-121(D) and § 19-141(C), the court construed the phrase "ensuing . . . election" in Oro Town Code § 2-3-6(A) as referring to the next permissible municipal election after the issuance of the initiative petition. Here, the initiative petition was issued on May 14, and the next ensuing election was the town general election on May 19. The initiative petition was null and void, as it was not filed 120 days prior to the May 19 election. Thus, appellant did not err in refusing to include the initiative on the statewide November 3 ballot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment finding that appellant town erred in refusing to include appellee's initiative on the next statewide general election ballot because the initiative petition was not filed four months prior to the ensuing general election after its issuance.

State v. Hoover


1 CA-CR 97-0685


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


195 Ariz. 186; 986 P.2d 219; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 223; 285 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



December 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on September 21, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-99-0064-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 96-07411. The Honorable Bernard J. Dougherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which entered a judgment of conviction for drive-by shooting in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 1209 (1997), after defendant was allegedly observed firing a gun at a house from a vehicle. The trial judge refused to give an instruction on endangerment as a lesser-included offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of drive-by shooting in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1209 (1997), after he was allegedly observed by police officers sticking a gun out of the window of a vehicle in which he was a passenger and firing at a nearby residence. The weapon was found on the ground near the scene of the arrest, and defendant confessed that he fired the weapon into the air as a warning to his nephew. The trial court refused to give an instruction on endangerment, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1201(A) (1989), as a lesser-included offense and refused to amend the standard reasonable doubt instruction. The court affirmed the conviction because there was no error in the trial court's refusal to instruct the jury on endangerment. The court found that endangerment by its nature was not always a lesser-included offense of drive-by shooting and that it was proper to deny the instruction. The court further found it proper to deny an amendment to the reasonable doubt instruction because the standard instruction was found to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for drive-by shooting because it found no error in the trial court's refusal to provide an instruction on the lesser offense of endangerment. The court found that endangerment was not always a lesser-included offense of drive-by shooting. The court found no error in the denial of defendant's request to amend the reasonable doubt instruction because the standard instruction was constitutional.

Clouse v. Department of Pub. Safety


1 CA-CV 97-0508, 1 CA-CV 97-0598, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


194 Ariz. 473; 984 P.2d 559; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 218; 284 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



December 15, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended By Order Filed February 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County Cause No. CV 96-00450 The Honorable Norman D. Hall, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, injured parties and their survivors, appealed an order of the Superior Court, Maricopa County, Arizona, which was entered against them after jury trial in their suit against defendants, police officers and the State of Arizona Department of Public Safety, Maricopa County, for negligence in allowing the release of a criminal who later committed crimes which caused their damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, injured parties and their survivors, filed suit against defendants, police officers and the State of Arizona Department of Public Safety, Maricopa County, after a criminal was negligently released and committed crimes that caused plaintiffs' damages. Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment in favor of defendant state, and defendant state appealed from the denial of sanctions under Ariz. R. Civ. P. 68(b). The court affirmed the judgment, and held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-820.02, which granted qualified immunity to public employees acting in the scope of employment unless they were grossly negligent, did not violate Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6. Further, the court ruled that the immunity statute was necessary to avoid a severe hampering of police work, an important governmental function. The trial court did not err in instructing the jury on a gross negligence standard of care, or in refusing to give the "acting in concert" instruction. Finally, the trial court properly denied sanctions against plaintiffs, pursuant to Ariz. R. Civ. P. 68(d), because unapportioned joint offers of judgment were invalid for purposes of Rule 68 sanctions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of defendant, State of Arizona Department of Public Safety, because the statute granting governmental immunity to public employees acting in the scope of their employment was not unconstitutional, and its grant of immunity was necessary to avoid a severe hampering of an important government function.

In re Jerry B.


1 CA-JV 98-0153


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


193 Ariz. 449; 973 P.2d 1210; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 210; 283 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



November 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on March 23, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-98-0596-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV-137678. The Honorable John J. Trombino, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which designated defendant as a repeat felony juvenile offender based on his admission of a new felony charge and placed him on juvenile intensive probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was a juvenile, admitted a new felony charge after a prior designation as a first-time felony juvenile offender. The lower court designated defendant as a repeat juvenile offender based on his new admission and placed him on juvenile intensive probation. Defendant appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that no ex post facto violation occurred based on an initial designation of defendant as a first-time felony juvenile offender under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-241(V) for an offense that occurred before § 8-241(V)'s effective date, because the impact on defendant was regulatory rather than punitive. The court also held that no ex post facto violation occurred when defendant re-offended and his punishment was increased as a repeat felony juvenile offender. When defendant re-offended, § 8-241(V) had already taken effect and defendant had been warned about the consequences of repeat felonies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the designation of defendant as a repeat felony juvenile offender based on his admission of a new felony and his placement on juvenile intensive probation, because defendant's designation as a first time felony offender for an offense that he committed by defendant before the effective date of the first-time offender statute was not an unconstitutional violation of ex post facto protections.

Duarte v. State ex rel. Lewis


2 CA-CV 98-0034


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


193 Ariz. 167; 971 P.2d 214; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 200; 283 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



November 25, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 307852. Honorable Jack T. Arnold, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which granted appellee state an 80 percent offset against damages awarded by a jury to appellants for injuries sustained when they fell from a scaffolding that appellee's prison officials had directed them to climb as part of their work. The offset was pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 31-238 for appellee's costs of appellants' incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoners fell from a scaffolding that appellee state's prison officials had directed them to climb as part of their work. Appellants filed suit against appellee, and a jury awarded them damages. Pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 31-238, the trial court granted appellee an 80 percent offset against the damages awarded to appellants to compensate appellee for its costs of appellants' incarceration. On appeal, the court affirmed, rejecting appellants' arguments that § 31-238 was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ariz. Const. art. II, § 31, and art. XVIII, § 6. The court held that the statute bore a rational relationship to the legitimate state interest of reducing the state's costs of incarceration and thereby reinforcing inmates' social accountability and fiscal responsibility for their crimes, such that it survived appellant's equal protection challenge. The court further held that the anti-abrogation clauses of the state constitution were not violated; because appellants were permitted to recover a portion of their judgment and their right of redress was not abolished, the statute did not grant de facto immunity to appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's award of an 80 percent offset to appellee state against damages awarded to appellant prisoners for their personal injuries, holding that the statute authorizing the offset was not unconstitutional under the equal protection clause of the U.S. Constitution nor under the anti-abrogation provisions of the state constitution.

Magellan S. Mt. P'ship v. Maricopa County


1 CA-CV 98-0025


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


192 Ariz. 499; 968 P.2d 103; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 208; 282 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



November 19, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 96-22666. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment to defendants, county and state department of revenue, on plaintiff's complaint challenging both the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44-221.01(A) (1997) and its applicability to plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a lawsuit against defendants, county and state department of revenue, that claimed the reassessment allowed under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42-221.01(A) for property with new construction violated equal protection and the uniformity clause of Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 2(1). On appeal from the award of summary judgment to defendants, plaintiffs claimed that the trial court erred in failing to postpone its ruling on defendants' motion and in denying plaintiffs' constitutional claims. In affirming the judgment, the court found that because plaintiffs' request for a continuance failed to comply with Ariz. R. Civ. P. 56(f), the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing a continuance. The court found that the reassessment allowed under § 42-221.01(A) for property that had construction improvements was based on the state's legitimate interest in taxing newly constructed property as soon as possible. Though it did not encompass properties with increased value due to rezoning and market factors, the court found no equal protection or uniformity clause violation because the latter were nonstructural changes which only minimally effected a property's value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granted to defendants, county and state department of revenue, because the assessment statute challenged by plaintiff taxpayers permitted defendants to reassess plaintiffs' real property up to September 30th of the tax year if new construction was added to it. The classifications established by the statute did not violate either the equal protection or uniformity clauses of the state constitution.

Inzunza-Ortega v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 98-0120


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


192 Ariz. 558; 968 P.2d 631; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 195; 282 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5

DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a special action, seeking relief from a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which rejected his civil complaint due to his failure to pay the court filing fee in advance under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-302(L)(2) (1998).


OVERVIEW: The trial court rejected petitioner inmate's civil complaint due to his failure to pay the filing fee in advance under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-302(L)(2) (1998). Petitioner filed a special action. The appellate court accepted special action jurisdiction because the case raised a constitutional issue of first impression and statewide importance and there was no adequate remedy in any other procedure or forum. 700 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Larsen v. Nissan Motor Corp. in U.S.A.


2 CA-CV 97-0181


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


194 Ariz. 142; 978 P.2d 119; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 190; 281 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



October 29, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 300722. Honorable Lina S. Rodriguez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which entered judgment upon a jury verdict in her favor but determined that appellee manufacturers were only eight percent at fault.


OVERVIEW: Appellant guardian's daughter was severely injured in an automobile accident where the car rolled over. Appellant brought an action against appellee manufacturer alleging a negligent design and strict liability. Appellant did not name the driver of the vehicle in the action, because as her daughter's employer, he was statutorily immune from liability under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-906(A). Appellee manufacturer did name the employer as a nonparty at fault pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2506(B) and Ariz. R. Civ. P. 26(b)(5). The jury returned a verdict for appellant but assigned only eight percent of the fault to appellee. On review, the court affirmed. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2506 was a permissible legislative regulation which, although sometimes reducing as a practical matter the damages which the plaintiff received, did not violate Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 31. The court found that the statutory allocation of fault system did not necessarily favor plaintiffs or defendants, but rather permitted the trier of fact to evaluate all of the evidence, including facts bearing on causation, and to allocate fault based on the jurors' collective concept of what was fair.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the Arizona constitution was not a guarantee of a particular amount of recovery, and it permitted regulations effectively reducing a plaintiff's recovery. The Arizona statutory allocation of fault system constitutionally permitted jurors to evaluate all the evidence, including facts bearing on causation, and allocate fault based on the jurors' collective concept of what was fair.

 

701 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Benitez v. Dunevant


1 CA-SA 98-0126


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


194 Ariz. 224; 979 P.2d 1017; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 188; 281 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



October 27, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 97-01169. The Honorable Thomas Dunevant III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED, RELIEF GRANTED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a special action to determine his right to a jury trial in his conviction by the Superior Court, Maricopa County (Arizona), for the criminal charges of driving while his license was suspended for driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with driving while his license was suspended because of driving under the influence (DUI), in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22-320(A) (1990). Petitioner challenged the constitutionality of the statute and also alleged that he was entitled to trial by jury. The lower court denied him trial by jury, holding that the offense was not one for which a jury trial was allowed under the constitution. After a bench trial, petitioner was found guilty and sentenced to 48 hours in jail, a fine, and suspension of his driver's license. Reversing and remanding the judgment of the lower court, the court held that considering the consequences of the offense, petitioner was eligible for a jury trial if properly demanded. The court further ruled that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22-320(A) (1990) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, because the consequences of driving while license was suspended for driving under the influence was a jury-eligible offense. The court also held that the law making the offense a crime was constitutional.

 

702 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Samaritan Health Sys. v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 97-0386


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


194 Ariz. 284; 981 P.2d 584; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 169; 278 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



September 24, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on May 25, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-98-0585-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-09815. The Honorable Donald F. Daughton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED, RELIEF GRANTED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hospital filed a request for special action, seeking relief from the order of respondent trial court that denied petitioner's motion for summary judgment, which argued that petitioner had statutory immunity from the lawsuit brought by a physician, the real party in interest, for breach of contract and wrongful interference with prospective contractual relations based upon his suspension from the emergency room call list.


OVERVIEW: A physician, the real party in interest, filed breach of contract and wrongful interference with prospective contractual relations claims against petitioner hospital based on his suspension from the emergency room call list. Respondent trial court denied petitioner's motion for summary judgment, in which it argued that it had immunity under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 36-445.02 because it was conducting peer review. Petitioner filed a request for special action. The court granted relief in part. The court held that petitioner's by-laws were a contract, and that it breached that contract by suspending the real party in interest without a hearing. However, the breach of contract claim was barred by § 36-445.02, which allows only injunctive relief on issues related to peer review. Further, the court held that the Anti-Abrogation Clause, Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6, applied only to tort actions, not to contract claims. The court ordered respondent to enter partial summary judgment for petitioner on the contract claim. The court denied relief on the wrongful interference claim, holding that the record as to that claim was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The court granted in part petitioner hospital's request for special action, because respondent trial court erred in denying petitioner's motion for summary judgment on real party in interest physician's breach of contract claim, as petitioner was statutorily immune. The court denied relief as to real party in interest's wrongful interference claim, as the record was insufficient for the court to make a determination.

 

703 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Yoshida


1 CA-CR 97-0658


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


195 Ariz. 183; 986 P.2d 216; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 166; 278 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25



September 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on May 25, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-98-0529-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 96-92230. The Honorable Louis A. Araneta, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for one count of aggravated assault on a peace officer, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1204(A)(5) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for aggravated assault on a peace officer, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1204(A)(5) (1996). Defendant appealed, arguing that the officer lacked authority to restrain defendant when she attempted to leave and that the officer used unreasonable force in the restraint. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction because the officer was acting in her official duties at the time of the assault and the officer used reasonable force in restraining defendant. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1204 encompassed all aspects of a peace officer's good faith performance of his or her job-related duties, even if the officer's actions were later found to be constitutionally unreasonable. Thus, even if the officer did not have reason to enter and remain in defendant's apartment and to detain defendant when she tried to leave, defendant could not prevail. The court held that there was substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding that the officer did not use unlawful excessive force in subduing defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated assault on a peace officer, because the statute criminalizing defendant's conduct protected the police officer in all aspects of good faith performance of her job-related duties, even if the actions were later found to be constitutionally unreasonable, and there was substantial evidence that the officer acted with reasonable force in restraining defendant.

McNutt v. Department of Revenue


1 CA-TX 97-0024


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


196 Ariz. 255; 995 P.2d 691; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 164; 278 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayers filed an action against defendant Department of Revenue, which sought to encompass within their alleged class all retired federal employees who paid Arizona income taxes on federal pensions during one or more tax years 1984 through 1988, and to whom defendant refused to refund those amounts on the ground that plaintiffs failed to make timely refund claims. The tax court held in favor of defendant, and plaintiff appealed. OUTCOME: The judgment of the tax court was affirmed, and the court held that plaintiff taxpayers' informal claim did not comply with the refund claim requirement under Arizona law for every federal retiree taxpayer for each year from 1984 through 1988.

State v. Proctor


2 CA-CR 96-0414, 2 CA-CR 96-0417 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


196 Ariz. 557; 2 P.3d 647; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 162; 277 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



September 8, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court.
Writ of certiorari denied Proctor v. Arizona, 530 U.S. 1250, 120 S. Ct. 2703, 147 L. Ed. 2d 972, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 4277 (2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Petition granted by State v. Proctor, 2003 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 159 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-40801. Honorable John S. Leonardo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged their convictions for conspiracy and for fraudulent scheme and artifice by the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) in connection with real estate transactions in which they engaged. Defendants argued that the fraudulent scheme and artifice statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2310, was vague, overbroad, and internally inconsistent. They also argued the trial court's restitution calculation was fatally flawed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants engaged in a real estate scheme wherein they purchased property by offering a combination of cash and vacant land. The value of the vacant land was grossly misrepresented. One of the defendants would offer to buy the vacant land for a small down payment and a promissory note, which was without recourse to him. The houses thus purchased were quickly sold for cash at prices substantially lower than what defendants had "paid" for them. Defendants defaulted on the notes. The appellate court rejected defendants' argument that the statute under which they were convicted was vague and overbroad because it required the perpetrator to obtain benefit though scheme or artifice but provided that reliance on the part of the victim was not a necessary element of the offense. The court rejected defendants' argument that the statute was unenforceable because it imposed criminal liability for certain conduct even where no corresponding civil duty. The court rejected defendants' argument that the statute was internally inconsistent. The court ruled that the restitution award was flawed because it failed to account for certain offsetting factors, such as the value of the vacant land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences. The court vacated in part the restitution orders with respect to both defendants and remanded the case to the trial court for redetermination of the restitution amount.

City of Tucson v. Rineer


2 CA-CR 97-0407


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


193 Ariz. 160; 971 P.2d 207; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 154; 276 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



August 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied January 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-56179. Honorable Cindy K. Jorgenson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant handgun owner sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court Of Pima County (Arizona), finding that appellee city's ordinance, Tucson, Ariz., City Code § 21-3(5)(2), which prohibited the use or possession of firearms within city parks, was not preempted by state law and did not violate the Ariz. Const.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court found that there was no legislative intent, either express or implied, to prohibit all local firearms regulation, in light of the plain language of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3108(A) and the implication of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3108(B), which evinced the legislature's intent to permit local ordinances relating to the transportation, possession, carrying, sale, and use of firearms. The court also held that Tucson, Ariz., City Code § 21-3(5)(2) did not conflict with the provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3108, which did not address the possession or carrying of firearms in city parks. Because the city's ban on firearms in its public parks was enacted for the promotion of public safety and for public welfare, which was a legitimate purpose, and was reasonably restricted to specific areas of the city, it was a reasonable limitation on the right to bear arms in defense of oneself as guaranteed by Ariz. Const. art. II, § 26. Handgun owner failed to demonstrate that the ordinance was unreasonable or overbroad, or that it impaired his ability to defend himself, because he could simply avoid walking through the park with his firearm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Wagner


1 CA-CR 97-0092


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


194 Ariz. 1; 976 P.2d 250; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 140; 275 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 37



August 13, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 94-92394. The Honorable Barbara M. Jarrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and attempted armed robbery and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without the possibility of release on the murder charge ("natural life") and to a consecutive seven and one-half year term on the attempted armed robbery charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his natural life sentence must be vacated because the portion of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-703(A) (Supp. 1997), which authorized imposition of the sentence, was unconstitutional under the U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Defendant also contended that his convictions must be reversed because the trial court admitted autopsy photographs of the victim that unfairly prejudiced the jury. The court stated that § 13-703(A) was not subject to analysis under the vagueness doctrine. The court determined that defendant had not proven that the absence of sentencing guidelines in § 13-703(A) created a "substantial disparate impact" on his portion of the class. The court concluded that the life sentencing provisions of § 13-703(A) were constitutional, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the autopsy photographs. Hence, the court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for first-degree murder and attempted armed robbery.

Simpson v. Comm. Against Unconstitutional Takings


1 CA-CV 98-0246


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


193 Ariz. 391; 972 P.2d 1027; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 129; 275 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



July 28, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on February 12, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court CV 98-402-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 98-04611 The Honorable Robert D. Myers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which ruled in favor of plaintiff property owner, found the corporation's referendum petition to have a rezoning decision referred to the voters invalid, and enjoined the City of Phoenix from holding the referendum election.


OVERVIEW: After the Phoenix city council rezoned two golf courses, a corporation circulated a referendum petition and obtained enough signatures to have the rezoning decision referred to the voters. After the city of Phoenix set the date for a referendum election, a property owner filed a lawsuit to block the election. The property owner argued that the referendum petition was invalid because the corporation attached to it the rezoning ordinance when it should have attached the minutes of the meeting at which the council made the rezoning decision. The court reversed the lower court's injunction order and remanded the cause for dismissal of the property owner's complaint. The council's decision was a legislative act. Because the council adopted the rezoning ordinance before it approved the minutes of the meeting at which it made the rezoning decision, the corporation correctly decided to comply with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 19-121(E), by attaching the ordinance to the referendum petition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the injunction order and remanded for dismissal of the property owner's complaint.

Hendel v. Salt River Project Agric. Improvement & Power Dist.


1 CA-CV 97-0329


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 125; 274 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



July 21, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. MOTIONS FOR RECONSIDERATION OR PETITIONS FOR REVIEW TO THE ARIZONA SUPREME COURT MAY BE PENDING. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Designated as a Memorandum Decision per Order Filed January 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 96-19699. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed the injured party's complaint for damages against defendant Salt River Project Agricultural Improvement and Power District (SRP) based on the injured party's failure to file a notice of claim as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821.01(A).


OVERVIEW: The injured party filed a complaint against the SRP alleging injury by electric shock that occurred when he contacted a power line. The SRP filed a motion to dismiss based upon the injured party's failure to file a notice of claim as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821.01(A), which required a party with a claim against a public entity to file a claim with the public entity within 180 days after the cause of action accrued, or the claim was barred. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss and entered judgment in the SRP's favor. On appeal, the injured party contended that the SRP was not a "public entity" under § 12-821.01(A), and that the notice of claim statute denied him equal protection by unequally burdening his right to file a lawsuit against SRP. The court held that the notice of claim statute, as applied to SRP, did not violate equal protection because it did not deprive the injured party of a fundamental right. The Arizona Constitution defined the SRP as a political subdivision of the state, therefore, the injured party had no fundamental right to sue the SRP. The SRP was entitled to the same privileges and immunities as other governmental entities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the injured party's complaint.

In re United States Currency in the Amount of $ 26,980.00


2 CA-CV 97-0119


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


193 Ariz. 427; 973 P.2d 1184; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 114; 272 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



June 25, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court April 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 315104. Honorable William H. Tinney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a summary judgment from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which was granted in favor of appellee employee in a forfeiture action. The state argued that no meaningful interference occurred because the government agents delivered the package to the employee before she took any steps to obtain possession of the package.


OVERVIEW: The state filed an action in accordance with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4301 through Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4315 against the employee following an incident in which money mailed to the employee's job was found. The state contended the money found inside the package was subject to forfeiture because it was used or intended to be used to facilitate the commission of various marijuana or narcotics-related offenses. Following a summary judgment that was granted in favor of the employee, the state appealed. The state contended that no meaningful interference occurred. The court reversed and remanded, holding that there was no constitutional violation. Further, the court held that the employee never possessed the package, sought to gain possession of it, or made any claim to its contents until four weeks after she had expressly denied any knowledge of the package. The court, therefore, concluded that the seizure was reasonable and that there was no unconstitutional interference with the employee's possessory interest in the property arising from the officers' actions. Additionally, the court found that the trial court erred in granting the summary judgment without an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment that found that the law enforcement officers had seized a package without a warrant and granted summary judgment in favor of the employee in a forfeiture action was reversed and remanded.

Ramirez v. Health Partners


2 CA-CV 97-0083


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


193 Ariz. 325; 972 P.2d 658; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 107; 272 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



June 23, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court March 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 308804. Honorable Bernardo P. Velasco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents and brother of deceased patient, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee healthcare facility, dismissing appellants' claim that arose out of the unauthorized harvesting of bone from the decedent under the Arizona Anatomical Gift Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 36-841 - 36-850.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, parents and brother of deceased organ donor, sought review of a summary judgment from the trial court that dismissed appellants' claim that arose out of an alleged unauthorized harvesting of bone from the decedent under the Arizona Anatomical Gift Act (Act), Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 36-841 - 36-850. The trial court's judgment granting summary judgment to appellee healthcare facility was affirmed because a person who acted in good faith in accord with the terms of the Act was not subject to civil liability or criminal prosecution. The court held that appellee's miscommunication of appellants' wishes by inadvertently including bone as a donated item did not automatically preclude the good faith immunity defense under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 36-847(C), 36-849(F). Further, the court held that there was no common law right of action to recover damages for more than negligent interference with a dead body in the organ donation context. The Act's immunity provisions did not offend Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6, because the state had a legitimate and compelling interest under the Act and did not violate equal protection principles under Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's granting summary judgment in favor of appellee healthcare facility, because appellee acted in good faith in accord with the terms of the Arizona Anatomical Gift Act and was not subject to civil liability.

Subsequent appeal at U S West Communs. v. Arizona Dept of Revenue, 199 Ariz. 101, 14 P.3d 292, 2000 Ariz. LEXIS 130 (Ariz., 2000)
Related proceeding at, Remanded by Citizens Telcoms. Co. v. Ariz. Dep't of Revenue, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 138 (Ariz. Ct. App., Aug. 26, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Arizona Tax Court Cause No. TX 96-00519. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Arizona Department of Revenue (ADOR) and counties, appealed the order from the Arizona Tax Court granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff phone company in its action to obtain a refund from the ADOR because of an alleged overvaluation of a portion of the phone company's property.


OVERVIEW: The ADOR valued the phone company's class 3 commercial property pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 42-793(A)(1), 42-793.01. The phone company claimed that its property should have been valued pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-793(A)(2). The phone company brought an action against the ADOR and the counties, and the tax court entered summary judgment in favor of the phone company. On appeal, the court reversed and instructed the tax court to enter judgment in favor of the ADOR and counties. Sections 42-793(A)(1), 42-793.01 applied to telecommunications companies that provided local services even if they had revenues from other sources, and § 42-793(A)(2) applied to telecommunications companies that did not provide local services. The phone company provided local services. The phone company failed to present specific evidence to show that §§ 42-793(A)(1), 42-793.01 violated Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the tax court's order that had granted summary judgment in favor of the phone company in its action for a tax refund. The court instructed the tax court to enter judgment for the ADOR and counties.

Shelby Sch. v. Ariz. State Bd. of Educ.


1 CA-CV 97-0075


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


192 Ariz. 156; 962 P.2d 230; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 104; 271 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



June 18, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-16643. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school and director sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which upheld appellee Arizona State Board of Education's denial of a charter.


OVERVIEW: The school applied for a charter, which the board denied on the basis of the director's bad credit rating. The trial court affirmed the board's decision, reasoning that, even though the law did not mandate the creditworthiness requirement, such a requirement was well within the board's discretion. The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded for the trial court to make complete findings of fact and conclusions of law. The court noted that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 41-1063 provided that decisions which fall within the board's purview had to include a concise and explicit statement of the underlying facts supporting the findings. The findings did not need to be detailed nor in any particular form, though the reviewing court had to be able to discern how the agency reached its conclusion. The court held that the requirement protected against careless or arbitrary action, facilitated judicial review, kept agencies within their jurisdiction, aided parties' preparation of cases for rehearing and judicial review, and prevented judicial usurpation of administrative action. The court also held that the school should be permitted to amend its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed in part. The case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to order the board to reopen the decision as to whether to grant a charter, allow the application to be supplemented, and make complete findings of fact and conclusions of law to support whatever decision it made.

 

715 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jensen


1 CA-CR 97-0205-PR


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


193 Ariz. 105; 970 P.2d 937; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 89; 270 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 49



May 28, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-75687. The Honorable David R. Cole, Judge. This Opinion Substituted for Vacated Opinion of May 19, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 81.



DISPOSITION: Review Granted, Relief Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied his third request for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was convicted of two counts of first degree murder, and under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-453 was sentenced to concurrent life sentences. His convictions and sentences were affirmed on appeal. The petitioner appealed the denial of his third request for post-conviction relief. The court granted the petition for review, but denied relief. The petitioner claimed that he was not precluded from raising his claims were based on a significant change in the law, which were exempt from preclusion. The court ruled that § 13-453 did not apply retroactively. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion in dismissing the petitioner's request on the basis of preclusion. Statutory changes to parole eligibility which would make a penalty potentially more lenient were substantive in nature and were not generally retroactively applied.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for review. The petitioner's request for relief was denied.

 

716 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Leyva


1 CA-CV 97-0250


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


195 Ariz. 13; 985 P.2d 498; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 79; 269 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



May 19, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on September 21, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-98-0538-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 90-03498. The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which, on remand of civil forfeiture proceeding, entered judgment against appellee individuals in the amount of $ 50,000. Previously a $ 20 million civil forfeiture judgment had been entered, but that amount was found to have constituted a second punishment in violation of the Double Jeopardy Clause.


OVERVIEW: The state contended that forfeitures pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(D)(6)(a) (Supp. 1997) did not constitute fines for the purposes of the Eighth Amendment Excessive Fines Clause, and thus, sanctions imposed did not require review for excessiveness. Further, the state contended that assuming review for excessiveness was required the trial court erred in determining what amount would be excessive. The court concluded that the forfeiture was not intended to remedy an immediate danger but to punish persons who had engaged in criminal activity. The court held that because several factors pointed to a deterrent or retributive purpose, the forfeiture under the statute was subject to the limitations of the Excessive Fines Clause. The court affirmed the $ 50,000 award, holding that allowing a judgment against the individuals for the total amount of proceeds from the criminal activity, which the individuals participated in, was excessive. The court held that considering the number of people who participated in the illegal enterprise, and the individuals' roles in the enterprise, the award for the total amount of proceeds was not proportional to the individuals' culpability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the amount of the civil forfeiture judgment against the individuals.

 

717 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wooten


1 CA-CR 96-0579


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


193 Ariz. 357; 972 P.2d 993; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 159; 294 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



April 30, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended Per Order Dated September 4, 1998.
Petition for Review DENIED on February 23, 1999 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-98-0424-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 94-03150. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that convicted him of the offenses of first-degree murder, burglary, and witness tampering.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced for first-degree murder, burglary, and witness tampering. On appeal, appellant alleged that a prescreening of prospective jurors deprived him of his right to a fair cross-section of the community, that the exclusion of evidence that someone other himself was the killer denied him of his right under U.S. Const. amend. VI to put on a defense, that it was improper to admit evidence of the victim's telephone call identifying him, and that it was error to deny his request for a Willits instruction. The court affirmed, holding that appellant was not denied his Sixth Amendment right to a fair trial because there was no showing that the jury was biased. The court held that the preclusion of a third party defense which identified another person as the killer was not prejudicial because there was no evidence connecting anyone else to the shooting. The admission of the victim's call which identified appellant at her apartment was admissible as a present sense impression. The court also found no error in the superior court's refusal to give a Willits instruction because appellant failed to make the requisite showing of prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order which convicted appellant of first-degree murder, burglary, and witness tampering because appellant was not deprived of his Sixth Amendment right to a fair trial, the preclusion of a third-party defense was not prejudicial, and there was no error in the admission of evidence or the jury instructions.
