State v. Guytan


1 CA-CR 96-0746


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


192 Ariz. 514; 968 P.2d 587; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 56; 266 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



April 7, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on December 7, 1998 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-98-0241-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 95-08243. The Honorable Daniel E. Nastro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) convicted defendant of first-degree murder, two counts of aggravated assault, and a drive-by shooting, sentencing him to a prison sentence of "natural life" for the murder conviction, two consecutive 18-year sentences for the assaults, and a consecutive term of 24 years for the drive-by shooting, enhancing his sentences for gang motivation under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(T). The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant fired several gunshots from a car in which he was riding, wounding two rival gang members and killing a third. He was convicted of one count of murder, two counts of aggravated assault, and one count of drive-by shooting. The superior court enhanced the non-murder sentences by three years each pursuant to § 13-604(T). The court held, inter alia, that 1) where a juror failed to show up for the second day of deliberations, the superior court did not err in substituting the alternate juror because this was permitted under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 18.5(h), 2) this did not violate the defendant's right to a fair and impartial jury because such action could be taken despite a defendant's objection under R. 18.5(h), 3) the superior court's instruction to the jury was adequate although it failed to instruct them to begin deliberations anew, 4) the enhancements under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(T) were improper because the prosecution failed to indicate that it intended to seek them before the jury was impaneled, and 5) this error did not require reversal of the convictions because the gang-related nature of the charges was apparent from the indictment and discovery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and the natural life murder sentence, modified the remaining sentences to reduce them by three years each, and otherwise affirmed the sentences.

 

720 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Graf v. Whitaker


1 CA-CV 97-0121


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


192 Ariz. 403; 966 P.2d 1007; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 47; 265 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25



March 19, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-07892. The Honorable Norman D. Hall, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for negligence by plaintiff driver, defendant driver sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed her appeal from an arbitration award in favor of plaintiff, claiming that she appeared and participated in the arbitration proceedings, both in person and through her attorney.


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff driver and defendant driver were involved in an automobile accident, plaintiff filed a negligence action which was assigned to mandatory arbitration pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-133. The arbitrator defaulted defendant on liability as a discovery sanction for her repeated failure to appear for a deposition, and awarded plaintiff damages. The trial court dismissed defendant's appeal of the arbitration award on grounds that in violation of Unif. R. P. Arb. 7(a), defendant failed to participate in the arbitration and waived her right of appeal. The court agreed, ruling that the record supported the conclusion that defendant did not participate in the arbitration; her attorney could not fulfill her discovery obligations without her cooperation. But the court remanded for a reconsideration because the trial court erroneously based its judgment in part on defendant's failure to appear at the damages hearing as well. Plaintiff did not claim nor did the record indicate that defendant had relevant testimony to offer at the hearing or obstructed its conduct to any degree by failing to accompany her lawyer to the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the appeal by defendant driver of the arbitration award for plaintiff driver because the trial court erroneously based its judgment in part on defendant's failure to participate in the damages hearing of the arbitration proceeding. Defendant's attorney appeared for her at the damages hearing, and nothing in the record indicated that her failure to appear with him obstructed the conduct of the hearing.

 

721 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Dobert v. Dobert-Koerner (In re Estate of Dobert)


1 CA-CV 97-0153


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


192 Ariz. 248; 963 P.2d 327; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 37; 264 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



March 5, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. PB 96-00804. The Honorable Gary E. Donahoe, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A statute provided that a court order dividing a marital estate rescinded any revocable disposition or appointment of property made by a divorced person to that person's former spouse. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) held that the statute deprived appellant wife of insurance proceeds upon the death of her former husband and awarded the insurance proceeds to the son. The wife and appellant insurance company sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the wife had standing to challenge the statute because it affected her expectancy interest in the insurance proceeds. In the dissolution decree, upon the agreement of the parties, the trial court awarded the insurance policy to the husband. The court held that the wife therefore lacked any reasonable basis for expecting that her beneficiary status would continue. Her interest in remaining the designated beneficiary was not unconstitutionally impaired by the revocation provision of the statute. The insurance company was obligated to pay the proceeds of the policy to the legal beneficiary. Any failure on its part to properly ascertain the identity of the beneficiary was not caused by the statute. The insurance company received "written notice" of the claimed revocation when it received a letter sent to it by the son's attorney. The insurance company was not prejudiced by receiving notice by first class mail at an office that was not its main office. Its actual notice of the divorce and revocation satisfied the substantive requirements of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

722 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Caretto v. Ariz. DOT


1 CA-CV 97-0318


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


192 Ariz. 297; 965 P.2d 31; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 21; 263 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



February 17, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County Cause No. CV 96-16971 The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which vacated an administrative law judge's order suspending appellee licensee's license for one year for refusing to submit to a second of two breath tests administered during duplicate testing, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-691(B) (Supp. 1997).


OVERVIEW: The court found that the admission of the first test result in a criminal proceeding, standing alone, did not preclude an implied consent suspension. An officer requested that the licensee take the second test, but the licensee instead asked to speak to his attorney. When the officer asked for the attorney's name and address, the licensee unaccountably remained silent. The officer then reread the implied consent admonitions and the licensee declined to take the second test. The court declined to read the disjunctive phrasing in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-695(A)(3) as a limitation on a testing officer's authorization to administer the breath testing methods described therein, but found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-691(A), (B) authorized more than one type of breath test. The court concluded that the officer had the authority to request that the licensee submit to the second breath test and that his refusal to perform the test justified an implied consent suspension. The court found that a reasonable person in the licensee's circumstances would have understood from the officer's warning that delay for any reason encompassed delay to await consultation with a lawyer.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the superior court's decision, reinstated the administrative law judge's order, and remanded to the superior court.

Pike v. Ariz. DOT


1 CA-CV 96-0443


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 14; 261 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



January 29, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. MOTIONS FOR RECONSIDERATION OR PETITIONS FOR REVIEW TO THE ARIZONA SUPREME COURT MAY BE PENDING. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended Per Order Dated February 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-10616. The Honorable Paul Katz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual was injured in a collision with a street cleaning vehicle owned by appellee state and driven by appellee employee. The individual and his wife filed a personal injury action against the state and employee. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) entered a judgment which dismissed the action pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821 (1993). The individual and his wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state's street cleaning vehicle which was driven by an employee collided with an individual. The individual and his wife filed a personal injury action against the state and employee. The trial court dismissed the action pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821 (1993). II, § 13, and because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821 was part of a referendum that had been previously rejected by voters. Lind v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 97-0318


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


191 Ariz. 233; 954 P.2d 1058; 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 9; 261 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



January 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on April 21, 1998 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-98-0129-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 97-14869. The Honorable Norman D. Hall, Jr., Judge. Tempe Municipal Court No. 96-160953-2. The Honorable Michelle O'Hair-Schattenberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) denied a motion to suppress the use of a portion of a blood sample taken by a hospital following the defendant's car accident, but prior to arrest or establishment of probable cause. The trial court denied relief in the defendant's complaint for special action. The defendant filed a petition for special action challenging the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 28-692(J) (1996).


OVERVIEW: The defendant was involved in an accident. Before any police arrived and before any allegation of probable cause, the hospital staff withdrew blood for medical purposes and at the same time took more blood than needed for medical purposes. They set the extra blood aside in case law enforcement requested it as a legal sample, which did later occur. The court held that the blood sample fell within the meaning of the language "for any reason" in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(J) (1996). It was taken for medical purposes. The hospital merely took enough blood so that it was not forced to either (1) inflict a second needle puncture in order to have enough blood for medical purposes after complying with a possible law enforcement request for a portion of it, or (2) face prosecution for refusing to comply. The hospital retained custody of the blood until the police requisitioned a portion of it. This indicated that all the blood was for medical purposes unless a portion of it was demanded for law-enforcement purposes. Only when the police requested and received the sample did it take on a legal purpose. Thus, at the time the sample was taken, its purpose was solely medical.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the defendant's motion to suppress the blood sample evidence, upheld the constitutionality of the statute as applied to the defendant, and denied relief.

In re Franklin V.


1 CA-JV 97-0121


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 3; 260 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



January 13, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. MOTIONS FOR RECONSIDERATION OR PETITIONS FOR REVIEW TO THE ARIZONA SUPREME COURT MAY BE PENDING. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied. Opinion Ordered Depublished by Amended Order September 24, 1998. As Amended January 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV 515283. The Honorable John L. Popilek, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which adjudicated him delinquent after a conviction for disorderly conduct in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2904 (Supp. 1997).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was charged with disorderly conduct and adjudicated a delinquent. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for dismissal finding that the juvenile's statements to police officers, though profane and loud, were not fighting words. The court found that the juvenile's statements did not inflict injury or tend to incite an immediate breach of the peace as required to prove disorderly conduct. The court determined that the statements by the juvenile were assertions of his rights, not an attempt to start a fight. The court found that the juvenile did not want to be stopped by the officer and did not believe that the officer had a right to stop him. The court determined that the juvenile was charged with disorderly conduct simply because he asserted his constitutional rights in a loud and profane manner. The officer testified that the people who walked by the incident just kept walking by or watched what was happening. The court determined that there was no evidence that the juvenile's statements were likely to cause anyone else to breach the peace.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the juvenile's conviction and remanded with instructions to dismiss the charges.

State v. McDonald


1 CA-CR 97-0322


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


191 Ariz. 118; 952 P.2d 1188; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 244; 261 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



December 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Redesignated as Opinion per Order dated January 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 96-04445. The Honorable David R. Cole, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County, Arizona, convicted defendant for keeping a house of prostitution, a class 5 felony. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3208(B) did not apply to a prostitute working alone, operating her business from her own apartment. Defendant claimed that terms in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3211(3) such as "providing financial support," "supervising activities or work schedules," and "directing or furthering the aims of the enterprise" indicated that the legislature intended the statute to apply only in those situations involving more than one prostitute. The appellate court found that the statute merely required that a person operate or maintain a house of prostitution; a finding that defendant performed every activity listed in the statute was not required. Defendant paid rent on the apartment, purchased advertising in certain publications, and scheduled her own appointments. Defendant therefore met the statutory definition of either operating or maintaining a house of prostitution. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3208(B) did not explicitly exclude prostitutes who operated and maintained their businesses from their own homes. The statute was not void for vagueness as it clearly proscribed defendant's conduct. The evidence of defendant's criminal conduct was overwhelming.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Brun


1 CA-CR 97-0056


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


190 Ariz. 505; 950 P.2d 164; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 217; 258 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



December 11, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 96-91288. The Honorable Louis A. Araneta, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, granted defendant's motion to dismiss a felony charge on grounds of presumed prosecutorial vindictiveness. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State moved to dismiss defendant's misdemeanor charge, and filed a felony DUI charge, which defendant moved to dismiss for prosecutorial vindictiveness. The State argued that the trial court erred in presuming vindictiveness, as no such presumption existed in the pretrial setting. The appellate court found in the record no additional facts to justify a presumption of vindictiveness. Defendant filed a routine motion to suppress statements and a demand for jury trial. It was unrealistic to presume that those assertions prompted retaliation by the State. Nothing the State did or did not do suggested a likelihood that it filed a felony charge in retaliation for defendant's routine assertion of procedural rights. The federal standard was now more tolerant of a prosecutor's pretrial decision to increase a charge than it was when an earlier case was decided.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Northeast Scottsdale Prop. Owners' Ass'n v. City of Scottsdale


1 CA-CV 96-0392


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 219; 258 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



December 11, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS BEEN DEPUBLISHED BY THE ARIZONA SUPREME COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review by Supreme Court Denied. The Court of Appeals Opinion shall be depublished, pursuant to Rule 111(g), Arizona Rules of the Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-08881. The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed their suit challenging approval of a revised site development plan after it found that appellants lacked standing and that adoption of an ordinance implementing a zoning change was not subject to the referendum power.


OVERVIEW: Respondent city approved rezoning of part of a planned community, which change included a stipulation that construction begin within 18 months. Respondent failed to adopt an ordinance until eight years later when approval of a revised site plan was sought. Appellant landowners unsuccessfully protested the revision. Their request for a referendum serial number was also denied. The trial court dismissed their petition for special action and the court affirmed. It found that zoning was not effective until a formal ordinance was adopted and that respondent city could adopt the formal zoning ordinance at any time after the rezoning was approved. The court found that the trial court erred in determining that the adoption of the ordinance was not subject to the referendum power as the city clerk exceeded her authority in refusing to issue a serial number. It did not remand the matter, however, because the referendum process should have taken place after the initial rezoning approval and therefore the time for referendum had expired. The court also held that appellants lacked standing, as they did not allege sufficient allegations of special damages to withstand a motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of appellant landowners petition for special action because appellants lacked standing to challenge approval of a revised site plan as they did not sufficiently allege special damages. It found that the trial court erred in finding the rezoning was not subject to the referendum power, but did not remand the matter because the time for referendum had passed.

Arizona Dep't of Pub. Safety v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 97-0307


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE


190 Ariz. 490; 949 P.2d 983; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 215; 257 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



December 4, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV96-18312. The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state challenged the judgment of respondent Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which enjoined the application of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3825 (1997) to real party in interest offenders declaring that it violated the Ex Post Facto Clause, U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10; Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 25.


OVERVIEW: Offenders committed qualifying offenses requiring registration as sex-offenders under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3821(A) prior to the enactment of the sex-offender community-notification statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3825 (1997). The superior court enjoined the application of § 13-3825 to offenders declaring that it violated the Ex Post Facto Clause, U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10; Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 25. The court found that superior court abused its discretion and ordered the injunction lifted because retroactive application was constitutional where the overriding purpose was protecting the community, not punishing offenders. The court determined that the statute was regulatory rather than punitive because (1) the incremental degree of disclosure beyond that required by § 13-3821(A) was not an affirmative disability or restraint; (2) there was no additional scienter requirement; (3) the statute was not a deterrent or retribution where the dissemination of accurate public information about past criminal activities furthered a legitimate public interest; and (4) the behavior required to bring offenders within the ambit of the statute, being released from prison, was not criminal.


OUTCOME: The superior court's injunction of the application of the sex-offender community-notification statute to offenders was ordered lifted, and the declaration that it violated the Ex Post Facto Clause was found to be an abuse of discretion.

State Comp. Fund v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 97-0055


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


190 Ariz. 371; 948 P.2d 499; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 205; 256 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 32



November 20, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 96-09635. The Honorable Brian R. Hauser, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Arizona State Compensation Fund challenged a ruling of respondent Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied its motion for summary judgment and found that it was not a public entity for purposes of the notice-of-claim statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821.01 (Supp. 1996). Real party in interest insured brought a civil action alleging that the state fund's misconduct caused it to pay improperly high premiums.


OVERVIEW: The state fund was an insurance company licensed to sell workers' compensation and employers' liability insurance. The insured was an employer that purchased liability insurance policies from the state fund. The court found that the legislature's enactment of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-986(E) demonstrated the state fund was a public entity, because the legislature would not have enacted a statute expressly identifying those statutes, applicable to other state agencies but not to the state fund, unless the legislature viewed the state fund as a public entity. The court held that the state fund was a public entity subject to the notice-of-claim statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821.01, and to the one-year statute of limitations, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821 (Supp. 1996). The court held that the insured's claim was barred by its failure to comply with the notice-of-claim statute. The court found that it was uncontested that the notice-of-claim statute's 180-day time period had expired.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to enter summary judgment for the state fund and to conduct any further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

731 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Torres-Mercado


1 CA-CR 96-0770


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


191 Ariz. 279; 955 P.2d 35; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 207; 256 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on May 19, 1998 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-98-0023-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 95-92254. The Honorable Brian K. Ishikawa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of drive-by shooting and misconduct involving weapons, the latter committed by discharging a firearm at an occupied structure in furtherance of the interests of a criminal street gang. Defendant was sentenced to prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions stemmed from an incident in which defendant was riding with friends in a car and fired a gun at an occupied trailer home and an occupied house. Defendant was affiliated with a street gang. On appeal, defendant contended that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 13-105(7)-(8) were unconstitutional because the definitions of "criminal street gang member" and "criminal street gang" were unconstitutionally vague. The supreme court held that defendant lacked standing to challenge the statute on the basis that it was unconstitutionally vague to others because he engaged in the proscribed conduct. The court also found that §§ 13-105(7)-(8) did not have a real and substantial effect on the right of free speech and free assembly. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing to give the jury a lesser-included offense instruction. The supreme court held that the crime of disorderly conduct was not a lesser-included offense of drive-by shooting. The court also held that the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on endangerment as a lesser-included offense because no rational jury could find the elements of endangerment but not drive-by shooting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

732 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


MECHANICAL v. SUPERIOR COURT OF ARIZONA


1 CA-SA 96-0239, 1 CA-SA 97-0012, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


190 Ariz. 364; 948 P.2d 492; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 204



November 18, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CV 95-19366. The Honorable Brian R. Hauser, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED,


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners requested special action review of the order of respondent Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) that denied their separate motions to dismiss real parties in interest's complaint to recover for injury sustained from environmental toxins caused by petitioners' negligent design and construction of a building. Petitioners alleged that the complaint was untimely and did not include an adequate Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2602 affidavit.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought a special action review of respondent superior court's denial of petitioners' motion to dismiss the complaint filed by real parties in interest to recover for injury sustained from environmental toxins. Real parties alleged that the injury was caused by petitioners' negligent design and construction of a building. The court granted special action review, but denied relief. The court agreed with another Arizona appellate panel that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2602, which required a complaint against registered professionals or contractors to be supported with an expert's affidavit attesting to the validity of the claim, failed to survive strict scrutiny analysis. The right to recover damages in court was a fundamental right, and § 12-2602 infringed that right. The court affirmed the superior court's determination that the complaint was timely served. Ariz. R. Civ. P. 4(i) gave real parties 120 days to serve process after filing the complaint. Ariz. R. Civ. P. 6(a) stated that time was computed without considering the date of filing, and excluded weekends from being counted as the last day. As the 120th day was a Saturday, service on the following Monday was timely.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioners special action review, but denied relief. The complaint was timely served upon petitioners, and the heightened pleading requirements for actions against registered professionals or contractors was an unconstitutional infringement on the fundamental right to judicial action to recover damages.

City of Tucson v. Woods


1 CA-CV 97-0503


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


191 Ariz. 523; 959 P.2d 394; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 201; 256 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



November 12, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County. Cause No. 320926. The Honorable Michael D. Alfred, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This is an appeal from an order of the Superior Court upholding a statute that allowed certain communities in Pima County near the city of Tucson to incorporate as towns without the city's consent.


OVERVIEW: The challenged statute, Arizona Laws, Chapter 204, § 2 (1997), only affected one county and temporarily suspended Az. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9-101.01, which allowed a city or town in the area of another community seeking to incorporate to either annex the community or grant it permission to incorporate separately. The state claimed that the city lacked standing to maintain the lawsuit. On appeal, the court held that the city had standing because it had a direct stake in seeing that Az. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9-101.01 was not suspended and that the city had a constitutional right to be free of any local or special law relating to incorporation that affected it adversely. The court also found that the suspension statute was unconstitutional special or local legislation because (1) there was no legitimate and rational basis for the law; (2) it did not must apply uniformly to all cases and to all members within the circumstances provided for by the law; and (3) it was not elastic, or open, not only to admit entry of additional persons, places, or things attaining the requisite characteristics, but also to enable others to exit the statute's coverage when they no longer had those characteristics.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

State v. Nihiser


2 CA-CR 97-0070


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


191 Ariz. 199; 953 P.2d 1252; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 175; 253 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 40



September 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition For Review DENIED.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-52042. Honorable Michael Alfred, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, which convicted of drunken driving related offenses, suspended his licenses, and, as a condition of probation, sentenced him to four months in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor and aggravated driving with a blood alcohol concentration of 0.10 or more while his license was suspended. The trial court suspended the defendant's sentence and placed him on probation for four years. As a condition of probation, the court imposed a mandatory four-month prison sentence. On review, the defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting the results of his blood alcohol concentration test because the state failed to disclose the name and qualifications of the person who drew his blood. The court rejected that argument and found that, since the defendant's blood was drawn in a hospital, it could be presumed that it was drawn by a medical professional as contemplated by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(F). However, the court agreed with the defendant that he should have been given credit for the two days of presentence custody. Therefore, the court affirmed the convictions and modified the sentence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's convictions were affirmed and the sentence was modified. The state did not have to provide the name and qualifications of the individual who took the defendant's blood sample at a because there was a presumption that such a person at a hospital was a professional.

Baker v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 97-0084, 1 CA-SA 97-0089, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


190 Ariz. 336; 947 P.2d 910; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 157; 251 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



September 9, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CR 96-13084 and CR 96-09161. The Honorable Stephen A. Gerst, Judge. The Honorable Peter T. D'Angelo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED  


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed special action petitions seeking application to their sentences of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01(A) (Supp. 1997), which the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) failed to apply. Section § 13-901.01(A) was part of The Drug Medicalization, Prevention, and Control Act of 1996 (Act), 1997 Ariz. Sess. Laws §§ 945, 946, which altered the statutory sentencing scheme and became effective on December 6, 1996.


OVERVIEW: One defendant was convicted of possessing marijuana, and the other defendant was convicted of possessing a narcotic drug. Defendants committed their crimes before the effective date of the Act but were found guilty after the effective date. They argued that because they were "convicted" of their respective crimes after the effective date of the Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01(A) (Supp. 1997) governed the trial court's sentencing options. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 1-246 (1995) was a clear and unequivocal expression of legislative intent that an offender's punishment was to be determined when he committed his offense. Furthermore, the court found that by construing "convicted" as defendants requested, the court would be construing the Act so as to render portions of it unconstitutional as an ex post facto law. The court concluded that § 1-246 controlled the applicability of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01(A) (Supp. 1997); therefore, § 13-901.01(A) did not apply to defendants.


OUTCOME: The court accepted special action jurisdiction but denied defendants the relief they sought.

Merrick v. Lewis


2 CA-CV 96-0085


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


191 Ariz. 71; 952 P.2d 309; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 145; 249 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 66



July 31, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY. Cause No. CIV 95043044. Honorable William J. O'Neil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona) granting defendant state's motion to dismiss his complaint against officials and staff of the Department of Corrections for loss of personal property. The trial court also ordered the inmate to forfeit five days' earned release credits.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the inmate's suit against officials and staff of the Department of Corrections for loss of personal property. It also ordered him to forfeit five days' earned release credits. The inmate argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 31-201.01(L), on which the dismissal was based, unconstitutionally abridged his right to petition the government by limiting his right to sue it, and to substantive due process because it denied him access to Arizona's courts. He also claimed the trial court improperly dismissed his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 civil rights claim because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 31-201.01(L) expressly allowed claims authorized by a federal statute. Lastly, he challenged the loss of earned release credits. The court partially affirmed. The inmate's loss of property did not implicate the right to petition the government. Furthermore, none of his claims alleged a § 1983 claim. The court also found that negligent loss of his property did not amount to a denial of due process. However, it reversed the forfeiture of his credits under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1604.10 because the legislature intended only prospective application; thus, it did not apply to him.

State v. Trachtman

738 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Musser


1 CA-CR 95-0849


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


191 Ariz. 228; 954 P.2d 1053; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 131; 249 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



July 29, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 95-00536. The Honorable Christopher M. Skelly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Arizona, which convicted him under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-2916(A) (1989), a statute that prohibited use of a telephone to threaten or intimidate. The defendant claimed that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad because it proscribed expression protected by the First Amendment to the United States Constitution and Ariz. Const. art. II, § 6.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued that § 13-2916(A) was so broadly written as to deter or constrain the freedom of expression of persons not before the court, and asserted standing to challenge the validity of the statute. The court found a colorable prospect of a real and substantial deterrence of legitimate expression under the statute, and exercised its discretion to grant the defendant standing to proceed with his claim. The court found that § 13-2916(A) swept in a broad array of constitutionally protected speech in the form of threats to the person or property of another. The court found that § 13-2916(A) was susceptible to arbitrary law enforcement and to chilling or deterrence of free speech. The court found that § 13-2916(A) was facially violative of the First Amendment to the U.S. Constitution and of Ariz. Const. art. II, § 6. The court declined to attempt a narrowing construction to the statute. The court found that a statute must provide a reasonable degree of guidance both to those who wish to confine their behavior to the law and those who must enforce the law and, to meet that need, the legislature had to rewrite § 13-2916 to redefine what telephonic conduct was proscribed.


OUTCOME: The court found Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-2916(A) (1989) unconstitutionally overbroad. The court reversed the defendant's conviction and sentence and directed the entry of judgment of acquittal.

Hunter Contr. Co. v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 96-0222


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


190 Ariz. 318; 947 P.2d 892; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 129; 248 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 40



July 24, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CV 96-03601. The Honorable Mark F. Aceto, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner contractor sought review of the decision of respondent Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which declared that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-2602 (1996) was unconstitutional and denied petitioner contractor's motion to dismiss real party in interest driver's negligence action.


OVERVIEW: The driver struck a barricade and filed a negligence claim against the contractor. The contractor moved to dismiss the complaint because the driver failed to file an expert affidavit as required by § 12-2602. On appeal, the court held that § 12-2602 placed the driver under a burden to which other tort claimants were not subjected. The court found that the statute: (1) required the driver to hire an expert where no expert may have been required; (2) limited the expert witnesses to other contractors; (3) required the driver to develop an expert case without the benefit of discovery; and (4) imposed these requirements as a condition precedent to filing the complaint upon the penalty of dismissal. Because the statute infringed upon his fundamental right to bring the action, the court applied the strict scrutiny test and held that § 12-2602 was not necessary or the least restrictive practical means to prevent frivolous or nonmeritorious claims against registered professionals and contractors. The statute burdened all lawsuits against contractors and registered professionals and the legal system already provided the means to filter out frivolous and nonmeritorious suits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that declared that the statute was unconstitutional and denied the contractor's motion to dismiss.

McComb v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 97-0139


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


189 Ariz. 518; 943 P.2d 878; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 122; 248 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



July 16, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended Per Order July 25, 1997. Petition for Review DENIED on September 16, 1997 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-97-0334-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CV 96-20787. The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant school district board changed from an at-large voting system to a single member or "ward" voting system under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-431, plaintiff school district electors challenged the validity of the ward system and election. The Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) held that § 15-431 was unconstitutional, invalidated the election, reseated the incumbents, and ordered a new at-large election. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed. The electors did have standing and § 15-431 was unconstitutional. Because the statute was race-based, the court applied strict scrutiny. The court found no compelling interest where the record contained no evidence of historic racial discrimination and the legislature enacted the statute in response to mere claims of discrimination. The state's interest in avoiding litigation was not a compelling interest. Section 15-431 also was not narrowly tailored. The statute failed to limit its reach to discriminatory voting practices. Finally, even if only § 15-431(B)(3) was unconstitutional, the statute fell because that subsection was not severable. Without that part of the statute, there was no means to determine which of the single member district seats would take office. Also, laches did not mandate dismissal of the electors' claims. The electors' actions of protesting to the Department of Justice and requesting an opinion from the Attorney General supported the trial court's determination not to apply laches. Finally, the newly seated board members were not validly elected and could continue to sit until their successors were validly elected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that the election was invalid because the ward voting system statute was unconstitutional in its entirety. Because of laches, the remedy was limited to ordering a future election.

Soto v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 97-0059


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


190 Ariz. 450; 949 P.2d 539; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 116; 247 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 45



July 15, 1997, Filed

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, filed a petition for special relief which sought review of his automatic transfer to the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) and the trial court's decision, which denied his motions to dismiss, for a reduction of bond, and for third party release, in the state's prosecution of defendant for forcible sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with three counts of sexual assault in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-1406 and -1401 for allegedly holding a victim down while another party assaulted her. The state contended that defendant committed forcible sexual assault, which automatically triggered his transfer from juvenile court to the superior court to be tried as an adult pursuant to Ariz. State v. Cisneroz


1 CA-CR 96-0392


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


190 Ariz. 315; 947 P.2d 889; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 112; 246 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 51



July 1, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on December 16, 1997 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-97-0310-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 95-10528. The Honorable Armando de Leon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of drive-by shooting and misconduct involving weapons. The trial court refused to instruct the jury that disorderly conduct was a lesser-included offense of drive-by shooting.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, from his vehicle, shot at four teenaged victims. He sought a jury instruction that disorderly conduct was a lesser-included offense of drive-by shooting. The trial court refused to give the instruction. The court affirmed on appeal, finding no error. The court found that disorderly conduct was not a lesser-included offense of drive-by shooting because disorderly conduct had a requirement that defendant intended or knew that his conduct would disturb someone's peace and quiet. There was no such element in the offense of drive-by shooting. Thus, one crime could be committed without necessarily committing the other. On another point regarding the disallowed impeachment of the victims, any possible error by the trial court was harmless in view of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below.

Encinas v. Pompa


1 CA-CV 96-0355


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


189 Ariz. 157; 939 P.2d 435; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 97; 245 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



June 10, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-03743. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which entered a default judgment against him on a Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act (RICO) claim filed by appellee employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured at work. The employer did not provide workers' compensation insurance for his employees and the employee filed a complaint against the employer alleging gross negligence, conspiracy to commit tax and workers' compensation insurance fraud, and RICO violations. The employee did not serve the attorney general with notice and his complaint within 30 days, as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-2314.04(H) for all civil pleadings alleging a RICO violation. The employer alleged that the employee's failure to timely notify the attorney general deprived the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction over the RICO claim. The trial court rejected the contention. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 13-2314.04(H) was a reasonable and workable supplement to court rules governing notice and service of process. However, the court found that in stripping the trial court of subject-matter jurisdiction for a violation of its procedural directives, § 13-2314.04(H) was antithetical to the purpose of procedural rules and conflicted with Ariz. R. Civ. P. 82. Thus, the court found the jurisdictional component of § 13-2314.04(H) void.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the employee in his RICO claim against the employer was affirmed.

Cutter Aviation v. Ariz. Dep't of Revenue


1 CA-TX 95-0017, 1 CA-TX 96-0001


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


191 Ariz. 485; 958 P.2d 1; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 85; 243 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 53



May 22, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause Nos. TX 94-00039 and TX 95-00026. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant airlines challenged the order of the Arizona Tax Court, which denied the airlines their separate actions for ad valorem tax refunds from appellees, county and state department of revenue, but denied the county's claim that the tax discounts under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42-162(A)(12) (1993) (class 12), and Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42-162(A)(13) (1994), (class 13), violated the Uniformity Clause, Ariz. Const. art. IX § 1.


OVERVIEW: The airlines paid ad valorem taxes to the county under protest, and when the county refused a refund, filed separate actions to compel the payment of the refund. The county claimed the discount given to possessory interests, under class 12 and class 13 treatment violated the Uniformity Clause. The tax court denied the refunds and the constitutional challenge. The airlines appealed. The county cross-appealed. The court reversed. The possessory interests were not class three commercial property under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 42-162(A)(3), -227(A)(3). The possessory interests were not owned by the airlines, because they were tenants and lacked the ability to dispose of the interests and therefore were class 12 interests, which entitled the airlines to their refunds. The classifications had not violated the Uniformity Clause because the legislature had made a valid attempt based on the nature of the property to tax property that was otherwise not taxable because the owners were tax-exempt government entities. Property tax classifications were definable by more than one limitation. The classification scheme was rational and not in violation of Ariz. Const. art. IX, § 2(6) or § 1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the tax court and remanded the case with instructions to grant the airlines the refunds they had requested, as well as their attorney fees.

Scottsdale Princess Pshp. v. Arizona Dep't of Revenue


1 CA-TX 95-0020


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T

Related proceeding at SHR Scottsdale X LLC v. Maricopa County, 2011 Ariz. Tax LEXIS 5 (Ariz. Tax Ct., Oct. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause Nos. TX 94-00013 and TX 95-00028. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.

OVERVIEW: The taxpayer leased a majority of the land its resort was located on from a city. OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court which granted judgment in favor of the state department of revenue and denied the taxpayer's request for a tax refund and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to grant the taxpayer a refund and any other needed special relief in the taxpayer's requests for a tax refund in the taxpayer's action challenging the constitutionality of tax statutes.

Nolde v. Frankie


1 CA-CV 95-0475


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


190 Ariz. 422; 949 P.2d 511; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 69; 242 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



May 1, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 93-16000. The Honorable Cheryl K. Hendrix, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former students sought review of a judgment granted in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), that granted motions for summary judgment by defendants, a teacher and a school district. Defendants' motions were based on the two-year statute of limitations for actions that alleged defendant teacher molested them.


OVERVIEW: Former students argued that the statute of limitations did not begin to run until they discovered the causal connection between their injuries and teacher's conduct. Former students also argued that a special tolling rule should be adopted for cases that involved the abuse of a child by an adult in a position of trust. The court held that precedent established by the state supreme court in another matter that was decided after former students' appeal was filed precluded a decision by the court in favor of former students. Because former students were capable of managing their ordinary daily affairs during the interval in which they were molested, they did not possess the requisite unsound mind required to toll the statute of limitations under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-502.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

State v. Singer


1 CA-CR 96-0403, 1 CA-CR 96-0701 (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


190 Ariz. 48; 945 P.2d 359; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 46; 239 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



March 27, 1997, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. LC 94-00039, LC 95-00841. Phoenix Municipal Court. Cause Nos. 8788487, 8834620. The Honorable Armando de Leon, Judge. The Honorable Bernard J. Dougherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The municipal court convicted defendant of two violations of Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 8-2 (1962) by keeping a dog which was in the habit of barking or howling, or disturbing the peace and quiet of any person. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) affirmed the municipal court's judgments. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the municipal court of two violations of Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 8-2 (1962). The superior court affirmed. On further appeal, the court also affirmed. Section 8-2 barred persons from keeping a dog which was in the habit of barking or howling or disturbing the peace and quiet of "any person" in the city. The court did not find that the phrase "any person" in § 8-2 was unconstitutionally vague. Because § 8-2 was not unconstitutionally vague, the court found that defendant's convictions were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's decision that had upheld the municipal court's judgment convicting defendant.

 

748 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Dugan v. Fujitsu Bus. Communs. Sys.


1 CA-CV 95-0223


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


188 Ariz. 516; 937 P.2d 706; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 40; 239 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 9



March 18, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended Per Order, Dated April 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 92-19208. The Honorable Michael O. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an employee who suffered a heart attack at work and her family members, sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, a telephone system manufacturer, whose system was used by the employer for whom the employee worked when the industrial injury occurred.


OVERVIEW: Unbeknownst to the employees, the employer had purchased from the telephone system manufacturer a system that blocked 9-1-1 service. Due to the inability to access 9-1-1 directly, emergency help was delayed when the employee suffered a heart attack, resulting in irreversible brain damage. The trial court granted summary judgment to the telephone system manufacturer. On appeal, the court ruled that although Ariz. Stat. Rev. § 23-1023(B) effectively limited to one year the period of time within which one entitled to workers' compensation could bring a third party claim, §12-502 applied to that limitation. Section 12-502 provided that if a person was entitled to bring an action was at the time of the cause of the action of unsound mind, the period of such disability should not be deemed a portion of the period limited for commencement. The court determined that since the employee had been rendered mentally incompetent by her industrial injury, § 12-502 tolled the one year limitation of § 23-1023(B) within which the employee could bring a third party action for damages. The court ruled that the time limit on the claims of the employee's family members was not tolled by § 12-502.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that granted summary judgment in favor of the telephone system manufacturer and against the employee. The court affirmed the trial court's decision that granted summary judgment to the telephone manufacturer on the claims asserted by the employee's family members.

 

749 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Phoenix Newspapers v. Dep't of Corr.


1 CA-CV 96-0255


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


188 Ariz. 237; 934 P.2d 801; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 38; 239 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



March 18, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-07262. The Honorable Frank T. Galati, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff newspapers sought a declaratory judgment that defendant corrections department unconstitutionally discriminated against members of the media by denying them prison visitation privileges. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) dismissed the claim based on res judicata and awarded bad faith attorney's fees to corrections department. Newspapers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court sharply criticized Arizona's same evidence test for finding res judicata, opining that a transactional test was more modern and preferable. Under the same evidence test, however, which was still in effect, newspapers' statement of slightly different facts and legal theory escaped the bar of res judicata. The court held, however, that there were no facts under which newspapers were entitled to relief. First, the state had a rational basis for excluding newspapers and others from prisons. Second, the Equal Protection Clause did not prohibit discrimination in favor of any group. The court held that the trial court erred in granting attorney's fees to corrections department, because the claim was not groundless; as determined above, the claim was not barred by res judicata. The trial court also failed to find that the suit was intended to harass the state, although it found it had a harassing effect. This was not sufficient under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-349, which required a finding of intent, groundlessness, and bad faith.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling that newspapers' complaint was barred by res judicata. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the complaint for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The court reversed the trial court's award of attorneys' fees to corrections system.

Defendant challenged the conviction contending that the trial court erred in denying his motion for judgment of acquittal, that the enhanced sentence was premised upon a statute that was overbroad and void for vagueness, that defendant's sentence and enhancement sentence amounted to double punishment, and that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. Pompa v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 96-0300


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


187 Ariz. 531; 931 P.2d 431; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 13; 235 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



January 30, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-03743. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Arizona), which entered a default judgment in favor of plaintiffs, employee and his wife. The employee filed a motion to dismiss the appeal for lack of jurisdiction, as the employer failed to comply with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(M). The employer filed a response to the motion to dismiss and petition for special action seeking dismissal for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: While working for the employer, the employee sustained an injury. The employee filed a complaint against the employee, alleging state Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act (RICO) violations and other claims. The trial court granted the employee a default judgment on his RICO claim. The court denied the employee's motion to dismiss the appeal and accepted jurisdiction of the employer's special action. The court held that the jurisdictional provision of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(M), divesting the court of jurisdiction for the employer's failure to serve the attorney general's office conflicted with court-promulgated procedural rules, Ariz. R. App. P. 8 and 15, and was, thus, unconstitutional under Ariz. Const. art. VI, § 5.The court-made rules of appellate procedure already permitted the court to impose sanctions for failure to serve proper notice on the necessary parties. The mandate in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(M) requiring automatic divestment of jurisdiction conflicted with those rules. The court denied the special action relief sought by the employer because he had an adequate remedy by appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the employee's motion to dismiss the appeal and accepted jurisdiction of the employer's special action. The court denied the special action relief sought by the employer.

 

752 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davila


2 CA-CR 95-0642


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


189 Ariz. 44; 938 P.2d 93; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 47; 238 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



January 16, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Redesignated as an Opinion March 7, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-48188. Honorable Howard Hantman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which entered his conviction, upon a jury verdict, for possessing a prohibited weapon, a sawed-off shotgun.


OVERVIEW: Defendant questioned the sufficiency of the evidence to convict him and the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(A)(3), the prohibited weapons statute. A weapon prohibited by § 13-3102(A)(3) included a shotgun with a barrel length of less than 18 inches under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3101(7)(d). A sheriff's deputy testified to the weapon's measurements using various points of reference, and his testimony established that the barrel measured approximately 15 inches in length. Thus, the court ruled that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The court also rejected defendant's contention that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(A)(3) was unconstitutionally vague because it did not define what constituted the "barrel" of a gun. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague because a term was undefined and susceptible to more than one meaning. The definition of barrel that the deputy sheriff used was consistent with a dictionary definition. Thus the court found no merit in defendant's attempt to include other portions of the weapon within the definition in an attempt to stretch the weapon involved beyond the common usage definition employed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Pimalco, Inc. v. Maricopa County


1 CA-TX 96-0002


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


188 Ariz. 550; 937 P.2d 1198; 1997 Ariz. App. LEXIS 4; 233 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



January 9, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause Nos. TX 94-00055, TX 94-00108 and TX 94-00975. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review from a judgment of the Arizona Tax Court, which granted summary judgment to appellee county and the department of revenue after taxpayers sought refunds of property taxes assessed on their leasehold interests in real property held by the United States government in trust for a tribal Indian community.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers and the tribe contended that (1) the tax court erred in finding that the leasehold interests constituted a possessory interest taxable under former Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 42-681 and 42-682; (2) Arizona's former possessory interest tax was invalid under federal Indian law; (3) the county's enforcement of the possessory interest tax violated the taxpayer's rights to equal protection; and (4) the taxpayers were entitled to partial refunds of possessory interest taxes. On appeal, the court affirmed the tax court's judgment that (1) the leasehold interest constituted a taxable possessory interest because the taxpayers obtained their leaseholds pursuant to an agreement with a governmental entity; (2) that the possessory tax was validly applied because federal law did not preempt the taxation of the leaseholds; and (3) that no equal protection violation occurred because the record contained no evidence that the county intended to or did treat other holders of taxable possessory interests any differently. The tax court erred, however, in denying refunds to the taxpayers based on the statutory reclassification of their possessory interests in the park as class 12 property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of refunds to the taxpayers based on the reclassification statute and remanded.

State v. Baldenegro


2 CA-CR 95-0561


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


188 Ariz. 10; 932 P.2d 275; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 269



December 19, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-48931. Honorable Robert B. Donfeld, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) convicted defendant of three counts of drive-by shooting, three counts of aggravated assault, one count of assisting a criminal syndicate, and one count of participating in a criminal street gang. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part defendant's convictions. Defendant contended that the trial court improperly instructed the jury on accomplice liability. The court held that if the jury believed defendant drove the car and his codefendant fired the shots, they could have concluded from the way defendant drove the car that he agreed to or attempted to aid in the offenses and was guilty as an accomplice. Defendant contended that there was a lack of evidence regarding two of the charges for aggravated assault. The court reversed the conviction on one of the charges because there was no evidence from which the jury could have concluded the victim was in reasonable apprehension of imminent physical injury. The court held that defendant lacked standing to challenge the gang statutes because he did not claim that his potentially innocent conduct was being prosecuted. Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion when it admitted evidence of gang activity by other gang members. The court found no error because the evidence had substantial probative value because it provided an essential element of proof that the gang was a criminal street gang.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction on one of the aggravated assault charges. The court affirmed the remainder of defendant's convictions.

Arizona State Bd. of Regents ex rel. Arizona State Univ. v. Arizona State Personnel Bd.


1 CA-CV 95-0478


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


191 Ariz. 160; 953 P.2d 904; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 218; 12 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 201; 227 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



October 8, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-07104. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) finding that the Arizona State Personnel Board did not have jurisdiction over employee's whistleblower complaint against appellee Arizona State University (university) because university's grievance procedure provided the only forum for her complaint.


OVERVIEW: The superior court determined that the Arizona State Personnel Board did not have jurisdiction over employee's whistleblower's action. Specifically, the superior court found that the state's whistleblower statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-531, did not apply to university because it would have been duplicative of the university's own policy and grievance procedure for such claims. The court affirmed. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-533 specifically provided that the whistleblower statute was not applicable to a state university where the university had a similar policy. University's policy was similar to the state statute and was, therefore, adequate protection of employee's rights. Additionally, while the university's policy did not include the right to counsel and did not vest the hearing officer with the ability to issue subpoenas, the procedures met the statutory requirements of Arizona's Administrative Procedure Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1001 et seq.


OUTCOME: The order finding that the Arizona Personnel Board did not have jurisdiction over employee's whistleblower action against university was affirmed because university had its own whistleblower protection policy and, therefore, the reprisal statute did not apply to employee.

In re Maricopa County Juvenile Action No. JV-132744


1 CA-JV 96-0041


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


188 Ariz. 180; 933 P.2d 1248; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 214; 226 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 34



October 1, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on March 25, 1997 by Arizona Supreme Court CV 96-0582-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. JV-132744. The Honorable Barbara R. Mundell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which required him to register as a sex offender pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3821 (Supp. 1995).


OVERVIEW: After the juvenile pled guilty to sexual contact with a minor, he was required to register as a sex offender pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3821 (Supp. 1995). The juvenile contended that the statutory scheme was unconstitutional because it permitted the juvenile court to exercise jurisdiction over him beyond his 18th birthday, impermissibly impinging on the confidentiality of juvenile proceedings, and was an unconstitutional ex post facto law. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the legislature could enact a statute which applied to juveniles who have been adjudicated delinquent and which required them to do something even after they reach the age of majority. The registration requirements of §§ 13-3821 and 13-3822 did not violate any rule of confidentiality. The information was only available to law enforcement agencies and was not included in the information available under the recently enacted community notification law. The overriding purpose of the statute was to facilitate the location of offenders and that purpose was unrelated to punishing the offender for past crimes. Thus, the statute did not violate ex post facto laws.


OUTCOME: The order which required the juvenile to register as a sex offender was affirmed.

Centric-Jones Co. v. Town of Marana


1 CA-TX 94-0025


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


188 Ariz. 464; 937 P.2d 654; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 209; 226 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



September 26, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 93-01368. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant partnership sought review of an order from an Arizona tax court, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee town thereby sustaining a final assessment of transaction privilege taxes made by appellee as to appellant's contracting income.


OVERVIEW: Following an audit, appellee town assessed unpaid transaction privilege taxes against appellant partnership on its contracting income. Appellant subsequently filed an action in tax court seeking review of the assessment. The tax court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9-240(B)(18) delegated appellee the authority to enact the privilege taxes as a condition of engaging in business within the town where towns had historically imposed transaction privilege taxes and related statutes reflected the understanding that towns had the power to impose such taxes. The court determined that the application of appellee's privilege tax on appellant's entire gross receipts from the project that took place in the town did not violate appellant's due process rights where the tax imposed was not out of all appropriate proportion to the business appellant transacted in the town. The court held there was a sufficient nexus between appellant's activity in the town and the taxes imposed because appellant had a significant presence in the town and enjoyed all the town services that any other taxpayer enjoyed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that granted a summary judgment in favor of appellee town. The court held that a statute authorized appellee to enact privilege taxes as a condition of engaging in business in the town where towns in the state had historically imposed transaction privilege taxes and related statutes reflected the understanding that towns had the power to impose such taxes.

In re Appeal Juvenile Action No. JV-512016


1 CA-JV 96-0036


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


186 Ariz. 414; 923 P.2d 880; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 202; 225 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 52



September 17, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. JV-512016. The Honorable Kenneth L. Fields, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) sentencing him to serve 24 months in a locked facility, rather than the 9-12 month term under the guidelines. The juvenile argued that by exercising prescriptive power over the juvenile's minimum length of stay, the juvenile court unlawfully gave retroactive application to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-241(I).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile pled guilty to attempted child molestation. As a term of probation, he was required to reside at a residential treatment center. The juvenile ran away from the treatment center and later pled guilty to failing to attend school. Although the guidelines recommended a 9-12 month term, the juvenile court sentenced the juvenile to serve 24 months in a locked facility. On review, the juvenile argued that because he committed his delinquent act in December 1994 and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-241(I) did not take effect until September 30, 1995, the juvenile court was precluded under the statute and under the ex post facto clauses of the federal and state constitutions from imposing a minimum period of commitment for an act that preceded the statute's effective date. The appeals court interpreted the statute as extending the juvenile court's prescriptive power over the term of confinement in dispositions after September 30, 1995. Since this disposition took place in January 1996, the juvenile court was statutorily entitled to draw upon § 8-241. The court ruled that the retroactive application of the statute was proper because it did not subject the juvenile to greater punishment.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the juvenile's sentence because the juvenile court did not err in applying the new statute retroactively since it merely regulated without increasing the penalty for an offense.

State v. McLamb


1 CA-CR 95-0329


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


188 Ariz. 1; 932 P.2d 266; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 204; 225 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 46

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 94-00904. The Honorable Bernard J. Dougherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant individual appealed from a judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which affirmed his conviction of a violation of Phoenix City, Ariz., Code § 23-21 proscribing the unauthorized wearing of the official insignia of the Phoenix Police Department.


OVERVIEW: Defendant individual contended that his conviction of a violation of Phoenix City, Ariz., Code § 23-21, which proscribed the unauthorized wearing of the official insignia of the Phoenix Police Department, was in error. The court's review was limited to the facial validity of § 23-21 because the action was instituted in municipal court and appealed to superior court. Defendant argued that § 23-21 was preempted by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2406, thus invalidating the ordinance. The court stated that the ordinance barred the unauthorized use of a public officer's insignia on clothing. In contrast, the statute prohibited the impersonation of a public servant with the intent to induce another to submit to his faked authority. The court affirmed, holding that there was no conflict between § 23-21 and § 13-2406(A). Contrary to defendant's arguments, the court held that § 23-21 was not vague or overbroad. Additionally, the court held that the city had a legitimate interest in regulating the use of its official insignia and the unauthorized use of it jeopardized the appearance of political neutrality and impartiality. Section 23-21 did not violate defendant's U.S. Const. amend. I rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the municipal code under which defendant individual was convicted was facially valid, did not conflict with state statute, and did not violate defendant's First Amendment rights.
