CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Arizona Department of Economic Security (DES) appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona), which denied DES motion in limine requesting dismissal of respondent grandparents petition for permanent guardianship involving dependent children.


OVERVIEW: DES petitioned for special action relief from the trial court's denial of its motion in limine, which had requested dismissal of a petition for permanent guardianship involving dependent children filed by the grandparents. DES stated that it did not consent to a permanent guardianship and that, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-525(B), its lack of consent prohibited such appointment. The trial court concluded that § 8-525(B) empowered DES to veto only the prospective guardians, but not the guardianship in general. Noting that DES did not object to the grandparents as guardians, the trial court denied DES' motion in limine. DES appealed, and the court affirmed concluding that the context of § 8-525(B) supported only the limited grant of veto over the prospective guardians. The court held that § 8-525 did not require DES' consent to the permanent guardianship itself.

Moran v. Moran


1 CA-CV 95-0437


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


188 Ariz. 139; 933 P.2d 1207; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 167; 222 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



August 6, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on March 25, 1997 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-96-0531-PR.
Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4781.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County Cause No. CV 95-90260 The Honorable David L. Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purported husband sought a judgment declaring that the marriage contract was valid and that a valid marriage existed between him and appellee purported wife. The purported husband appealed the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found and declared that the marriage was not valid and the contract between the parties was not enforceable as a marriage contract.


OVERVIEW: The purported husband argued that his marriage contract created a legal marriage and that Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 25-111, 25-121 was invalid because the requirement of a marriage license interfered with his free exercise of religion. The trial court entered a default judgment and the purported wife sought to set aside the default. The court found that the purported husband was not legally entitled to the declaratory judgment he sought and that the marriage was invalid. The marriage license requirement did not conflict with the purported husband's exercise of his religion because obtaining a marriage license would not infringe on his ability to solemnize the marriage in a religious ceremony or to observe his religious beliefs within the marriage. The terms of the marriage contract were unenforceable because the contract did not establish a marriage. The purported husband was required to establish paternity before he could seek custody of his child. The entry of default against the purported wife operated as an admission of the facts, but the trial court could not have declared that the parties' marriage contract formed a valid marriage where it would have been contrary to Arizona law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order declaring that the parties' marriage was not valid.

 

763 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 95-0340


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


187 Ariz. 411; 930 P.2d 488; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 157; 221 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



July 23, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on January 14, 1997 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-96-0498-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. JV-511263. The Honorable Kirkby Roseveare, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought a special action following an order of respondent Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 8-241(N), requiring the trial court to order human immunodeficiency virus (HIV) testing of a juvenile sex offender upon request of the victim, violated the Fourth Amendment's prohibition against unreasonable searches and seizures.


OVERVIEW: A juvenile was adjudicated delinquent on a charge of child molestation. The sexual act possibly exposed the victim to the juvenile's bodily fluids, and the victim's mother requested that the juvenile be tested pursuant to § 8-241(N) for the presence of HIV. The trial court rejected the request, finding that an involuntary test for HIV was an unreasonable search under the Fourth Amendment and that any testing for HIV should be performed on the victim. The state appealed and the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings, concluding that the statute did not involve an unconstitutional search. The court determined that the use of an order instead of a warrant to implement the test was not a Fourth Amendment violation because the issuance of the order required the same judicial scrutiny that would be required of a warrant. The court held that the lack of a probable cause requirement was not unconstitutional because the hidden nature of the disease required that a test for its existence was subordinated to the special needs of the state. The statute bore a substantial relationship to the state's goal of assisting victims of sexual offenses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that found the statute requiring HIV testing on juvenile sex offenders at the request of the victim to be unconstitutional and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

764 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal in Maricopa County Juvenile Action No. Jv-511237


1 CA-JV 95-0093


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


189 Ariz. 18; 938 P.2d 67; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 159; 221 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 42



July 23, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. JV-511237. The Honorable John Popilek, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: VACATED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found him delinquent after he admitted having rubbed his brother's penis while watching a video and, as terms of his probation, required that he be tested for human immunodeficiency virus (HIV) pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-241N and prohibited him from patronizing any place where sexually stimulating or oriented material was available.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 14 at the time of the offense and the victim, his brother, was five years old. The court held that § 8-241(N) did not violate the Fourth Amendment prohibition against unreasonable searches and seizures when the juvenile's conduct could have possibly resulted in the transmission of HIV. The issue of unconstitutionally broad application of § 8-241(N) was not framed for decision here because defendant's broader admission to a juvenile probation officer, which the trial court was entitled to consider, included acts that may have exposed the victim to defendant's bodily fluids. However, the court held that: (1) HIV testing should not have been imposed because neither the victim nor the victim's parent or guardian requested testing, as required by § 8-241(N); and (2) the trial court's directive prohibiting defendant from patronizing any place where sexually stimulating or oriented material or entertainment was available was void for vagueness because many convenience stores, movie rental establishments, and multiplex movie theaters would have fallen within the broad language of the trial court's proscription.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order requiring defendant to undergo HIV testing as a condition of probation, found that the probation condition prohibiting defendant from patronizing any place with sexually stimulating or oriented material or entertainment was unconstitutionally vague, remanded to permit the trial court to impose this term more narrowly drawn if it chose to do so, and found no infirmity in the remaining terms of probation.

 

765 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Lerma v. Keck


1 CA-CV 95-0555


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


186 Ariz. 228; 921 P.2d 28; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 151; 221 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



July 16, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 93-05731. The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a hotel employee, was injured by the willful and wanton conduct of defendant hotel guests, filed a civil suit, and obtained a damage award in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona). Based on new case law, the trial court then found that the award could be reduced by the hotel's comparative negligence and granted the guests' motion for a new trial. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict was granted because the guests was not entitled to comparative negligence for their willful and wanton conduct. The state's supreme court then issued an opinion that willful and wanton defendants were entitled to the benefits of comparative negligence under the state's Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act (UCATA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-2501 to 2509. The trial court then entered the original judgment. The court affirmed and held that: (1) the employee had standing to challenge Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2505(A) because she was injured by its operation; (2) the employee was not a member of a suspect class; (3) the UCATA did not impinge on a fundamental right because it affected only a claimant's ability to collect damages, not the right to bring an action, which was protected under Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 6; (4) under the rational basis test, the UCATA did not violate the state's equal protection clause, Ariz. Const. art. II, § 13; and (5) Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2505(A) defined a class of persons, treated them all alike, and was not special legislation in violation of Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's entry of judgment in favor of the employee based on the comparative negligence of the hotel and the guests.

 

766 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


2 CA-CR 95-0169


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


188 Ariz. 263; 935 P.2d 841; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 212; 227 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



July 11, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Redesignated as Opinion September 5, 1996.
Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-43338. Honorable Philip Fahringer, Judge (Retired).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) convicted defendant of one count of child abuse and one count of first degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose after his girlfriend's daughter died of apparent non-accidental head trauma or "shaken baby syndrome." Defendant argued, inter alia, that he did not have "the care or custody" of the child so as to be convicted for child abuse for failing to seek medical care for her in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3623(B). The court affirmed defendant's conviction. There was more than sufficient evidence to find that defendant had "care" of the child because he voluntarily assumed responsibility for providing for the child, referred to her as his daughter, and assumed the role of primary care giver by dominating the child's mother and controlling all their income. The court also rejected defendant's argument that his conviction for felony murder should fail because a crime of omission could not serve as a predicate felony for felony murder. The use of the word "acting" in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1105, the felony murder statute, did not preclude crimes of omission when defendant had committed an offense that the legislature had specifically included as a basis for felony murder.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions of one count of child abuse and one count of first degree murder were affirmed.

 

767 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


SCHABEL v. DEER VALLEY UNIFIED SCH. DIST. NO. 97


1 CA-CV 94-0274


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


186 Ariz. 161; 920 P.2d 41; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 143; 220 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 59



July 9, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 93-07536. The Honorable Michael O. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, student and his parents, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed, on motion, the complaint alleging that appellees, school and district, created an unreasonable and foreseeable risk of harm to the student by failing to maintain the school's playground, upon the court's determination that the school and district were immune under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.01 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The lower court had held that school and district enjoyed absolute immunity under the statute because the failure to install cushioning under the swing set was a discretionary decision concerning the allocation of resources. On appeal, the student and his parents argued that the school and district were not immune from suit, as they had a common law duty to ensure that the facility did not pose an unreasonable risk of harm once the decision to provide playground equipment was made. The school and district argued that § 12-820.01 provided immunity for acts that involved determinations of whether to provide resources for the purchase of equipment. The appellate court held that statutory immunity did not protect the school and district because they did not have the discretion to breach their duty to refrain from subjecting district students to unreasonable risks of harm. The appellate court noted that § 12-820.01 did not answer the question of liability in the case, as the legislative intent to extend immunity to all resource allocation decisions was not apparent. However, under the common law, the school and district had a duty to make the premises safe for the students.


OUTCOME: Although the appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the claim for negligent supervision, it reversed the dismissal of the claims concerning the condition of the school playground premises and remanded those claims for further proceedings.

 

768 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re 1988 Chevrolet 1/2 PU


2 CA-CV 95-0251


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


186 Ariz. 419; 924 P.2d 109; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 115; 217 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 44



May 28, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C-304834. Honorable Bernardo P. Velasco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant truck owner challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which found for appellee State in the owner's action for return of the truck, which was seized by the State. The State claimed that the court lacked jurisdiction over the matter pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(M), but the owner claimed that her appeal was perfected pursuant to Ariz. R. Civ. App. P. 8(a).


OVERVIEW: The superior court ordered forfeiture of the owner's truck after the owner's brother was stopped while speeding in the truck and a marijuana was found in the truck. The owner claimed that she neither knew nor should have known that the brother was going to carry marijuana in the truck. The owner appealed the superior court's decision, but the court dismissed the appeal for want of jurisdiction. The court explained that the owner had failed to serve a copy of her notice of appeal and a copy of her brief on the attorney general when she filed her brief with the court, as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(M). Hence, the court lacked jurisdiction over the appeal. Ariz. R. Civ. App. P. 8(a) did not apply, the court added, because Rule 8(a) only applied when the court had jurisdiction over the underlying subject matter. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(M) did not unconstitutionally undermine the court's authority to make rules and that the requirement of sending copies of the notice of appeal and brief was not an unreasonable barrier to the owner's appeal.


OUTCOME: The court found for the State and dismissed the owner's appeal.

 

769 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Scott


1 CA-CR 95-0101


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


186 Ariz. 503; 924 P.2d 507; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 103; 216 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 100



May 16, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 13, 1996. Petition for Review Granted on September 24, 1996 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-96-0347-PR. Pursuant to an Arizona Supreme Court order dated December 6, 1996 the order granting review is vacated and the petition for review is denied.
Petition for Review Denied December 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Coconino County. Cause No. CR-94-18690. The Honorable Fred Newton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of sale of a narcotic drug at the conclusion of a jury trial. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying him probation without a finding by the jury on the threshold amount of drugs sold.


OVERVIEW: Trial testimony demonstrated that defendant made separate sales of crack cocaine base. Defendant was found guilty of sale of a narcotic drug under two counts. At sentencing, the prosecutor urged the trial court to deny probation because, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408(D), defendant had sold a threshold amount of cocaine base, making him ineligible for probation. The trial court denied probation. Defendant alleged that because the finding of the threshold amount of cocaine was not determined by the jury, his convictions and sentences were unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that the finding of threshold amount was appropriately found by the trial court as a sentencing factor. The court noted that it was within the sole power of the legislature to prescribe punishment for criminal acts. Section 13-3408(D) simply dictated the weight to be given to the aggravating factor of threshold amount once defendant had been convicted of sale of a narcotic drug. The presence or absence of that factor did not modify the term of years for which defendant could be sentenced. The factor did not determine the class of felony and did not become a factor until after conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

770 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Mazen v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 95-0355


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 104; 216 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 97



May 16, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. MOTIONS FOR RECONSIDERATION OR PETITIONS FOR REVIEW TO THE ARIZONA SUPREME COURT MAY BE PENDING. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 95-05456. The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a special action contesting a decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied his motion to suppress evidence of marijuana taken from his storage unit in the aftermath of a fire.


OVERVIEW: The fire department extinguished a fire emanating from a storage unit. While in the unit, they saw several plants they recognized as marijuana. An officer, who was called to the scene, could see the marijuana through the open door. Because he believed they were in plain view, he entered without a warrant and seized the plants. He also seized bags containing marijuana. Defendant was arrested and filed a motion to suppress the evidence. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant filed a special action contesting the denial of his motion to suppress. Because the action involved a constitutional issue of first impression in Arizona, the court accepted jurisdiction. The court held that: (1) the fact that the officer saw contraband in plain view did not allow him, absent exigent circumstances, to enter the unit without a warrant; (2) where the fire was extinguished and the marijuana was in no danger of being destroyed, there were no exigent circumstances permitting a warrantless entry; and (3) where the firefighters did not have authority to seize evidence of non-arson-related criminal activity, the police could not "step in their shoes" and seize the marijuana.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

City of Glendale v. Aldabbagh


1 CA-CV 95-0401


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


187 Ariz. 235; 928 P.2d 659; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 97; 216 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 76



May 7, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 94-17918. The Honorable Louis A. Araneta, Judge. The Honorable Roger W. Kaufman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa (Arizona), which in an action for a declaratory judgment, ordered the city to issue a requested zoning clearance to appellees club owners and operators. After a nuisance action was resolved, the city did not issue a license to reopen the business, claiming abandonment of the club under Glendale, Az. Zoning Ordinance § 7(d).


OVERVIEW: After the city amended its zoning ordinance, the club continued its operations as a legal, non-conforming use. The county seized and possessed the club for 18 months, during which period the owners sent notice to the city of their intent to continue operating the club as a legal, non-conforming use. After recovering possession, the operators were denied a license because the city refused to provide the zoning clearance, claiming that the club had lost its legal, non-conforming use status. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment and held that under Glendale, Az. Zoning Ordinance § 7(d), one year of non-use created a rebuttable presumption that the owner intended to abandon the non-conforming use. The parties have stipulated that the club owners and operators did not intend to continue to abandon this non-conforming use. To interpret § 7(d) otherwise would deprive owners of non-conforming uses without due process of law guaranteed by the Fifth Amendment and the Eleventh Amendment. The non-conforming use would never have been abandoned without the efforts of government law enforcement officials.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court decision ordering the city to issue a zoning clearance to club owners and operators.

State v. Cameron


1 CA-CR 95-0321


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D

April 25, 1996, Filed

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed defendant's conviction of public sexual indecency, and the city magistrate's order which required defendant to register as a sex offender pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3821.


OVERVIEW: Defendant masturbated in a park rest room in the presence of an undercover police officer. He was convicted of public sexual indecency, a violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1403(A)(1). He alleged that the registration requirement, as applied to misdemeanor offenses, constituted cruel and unusual punishment or was an unconstitutional ban on travel. The court disagreed with both arguments and held that the Arizona Supreme Court, based on a decision by the United States Supreme Court, had determined that the registration requirement was not punishment. The court held that the requirement was not so excessive in relation to its non-punitive purposes that it had to be considered a punishment. The court also held that although the right to travel was fundamental, it was subject to limitations based on the legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Kerr v. Waddell


1 CA-TX 92-0010


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of decision entered in the Tax Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied them tax refunds and declaratory and injunctive relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983(1981).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought injunctive and declaratory relief, alleging that Arizona's income tax statutes were unconstitutional because they excluded from taxation the retirement contributions of state and local government employees, while they taxed the retirement contributions of federal employees. On appeal, the court concluded that the tax court lacked jurisdiction and reversed and remanded the case to the tax court. The court reversed its earlier opinion and held that the taxpayers' § 1983 claims were subject to administrative remedies before the taxpayers filed suit in tax court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the tax court's decision and remanded the taxpayers' lawsuit with directions to dismiss the lawsuit.

Estate of Bohn v. Scott


1 CA-TX 94-0009


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


185 Ariz. 284; 915 P.2d 1239; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 74; 214 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 51



April 16, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 89-00050. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers, who were retired federal employees, spouses, or representatives, appealed from a judgment entered by the Arizona Tax Court, which dismissed their complaint without prejudice, vacated their attorney fee award, and granted defendant Department of Revenue (Arizona) (DOR) an attorney fee award, in an action based on Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 43-1022(2)-(4) alleging discrimination against recipients of federal retirement income.


OVERVIEW: The lower court entered formal judgment on mandate dismissing the taxpayers' complaint without prejudice due to lack of subject matter jurisdiction because plaintiffs did not exhaust administrative remedies. On appeal, the court reaffirmed the implicit holding of a decided case that the taxpayers' request for declaratory relief was an integral link in their bid for recovery of refunds and was therefore barred by their failure to resort to and exhaust administrative remedies. The court found the DOR's cross-appeal properly encompassed all relief the lower court granted pursuant to the taxpayers' second amended complaint. This relief included the fee award. The court's reversal of the taxpayers' bid for court-ordered refunds and declaratory relief necessarily ended their status as "prevailing parties" under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-348. Thus the lower court did not err in dismissing the taxpayers' complaint on remand, or in declining to conduct further proceedings with a view toward granting additional relief based on occurrences post-dating the decided case. But the tax court erred in awarding attorney fees against the taxpayers pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OUTCOME: The court remanded with directions to modify the judgment to delete the award of attorney fees against the taxpayers.

State v. Taggart


1 CA-CR 94-0926


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


186 Ariz. 569; 925 P.2d 710; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 70; 214 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



April 11, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 94-90907. The Honorable Christopher M. Skelly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) after he was convicted of two counts of aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant rode his bike up to the victims, shined a flashlight in their eyes, brandished a knife, and told them to give him everything they had. The victims rode off, and defendant told them that he "had" the wrong guys. The victims called the police, and defendant was apprehended because he fit the victims' description of the assailant. At trial, defendant maintained that he mistook the victims for his friends. One of the victims refused defense counsel's request for a pretrial interview. On cross-examination, defense counsel asked the victim whether he had refused a pretrial interview. The trial court sustained the state's objection. Defendant argued that the restriction on cross-examination violated his right to confrontation. The court found that the restriction on cross-examination had violated defendant's right to confrontation because the victim's refusal to be interviewed may have reflected on the victim's credibility. However, the court affirmed the judgment, finding harmless error. Specifically, the victims' testimony was plausible, consistent, and partially corroborated by defendant's own admissions; in short, the evidence of defendant's guilt was very strong.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction in defendant's trial for aggravated assault. The court modified the judgment to remove an improper reference from the trial court's minute entry.

State v. Riggs


1 CA-CR 94-0970


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


186 Ariz. 573; 925 P.2d 714; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 71; 214 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



April 11, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-93-93493. The Honorable Daniel A. Barker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) entered an order convicting defendant of six counts of forgery and sentenced him to eight years imprisonment for each count. Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that business records and expert testimony were improperly admitted into evidence at his trial and that his right to confrontation was violated when he was not permitted to examine a victim about the victim's refusal to allow a pre-trial interview. With respect to defendant's objection regarding the admission of the bank statements and the signature card, the court held that whether the records were sufficiently reliable to be admitted was left to the sound discretion of the trial court. Moreover, the court found that because the statements evidenced that there were insufficient funds in the bank account, and defendant had already admitted there were insufficient funds any error was harmless. Moreover, the court held that the bank employee's opinion with respect to the forged signatures was properly admitted and insignificant. Lastly, the court found that defendant's inquiry into the victim's exercise of the right to decline a pre-trial interview was improper because it would be fundamentally unfair to allow the victim's exercise of this constitutional right to be burdened by consequent attacks at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State ex rel. Fox v. New Phoenix Auto Auction


1 CA-CV 94-0253, 1 CA-CV 94-0323 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


185 Ariz. 302; 916 P.2d 492; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 66; 214 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



April 9, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CV 93-20475. The Honorable Robert L. Gottsfield, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant used car dealer sought review of the decision from the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by the environmental quality department in an action against the used car dealer for delivering vehicles to customers that had not passed emissions inspections.


OVERVIEW: The state environmental quality department filed an action against the used car dealer alleging that the dealer delivered eight vehicles to customers that had not passed emissions and tampering inspections. The department filed a motion for partial summary judgment which the trial court granted. The dealer contended that its fleet inspector had inspected and passed the vehicles. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment. The court held that: (1) Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 49-542(D) did not expressly require that the inspections be certified or otherwise documented; (2) the court was not precluded from considering the dealer's evidence of inspection because it was not part of the "official" records, i.e., a validated inspection certificate; (3) a reasonable trier of fact could find that the dealer properly inspected the vehicles and thus the trial court erred in granting partial summary judgment; and (4) the civil penalties of § 49-550(F) are not applicable to other dealer violations of art. 5, including § 49-542(D).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the department and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

State v. Taylor


1 CA-CR 95-0260


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


187 Ariz. 567; 931 P.2d 1077; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 67; 214 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



April 9, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 11, 1996. Supplemental Opinion of September 10, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 192. Motion for Reconsideration Denied September 10, 1996.
Petition for Review DENIED on February 26, 1997 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-96-0611-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yuma County. Cause No. 19941, 19586, 19600. The Honorable Thomas A. Thode, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, REMANDED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order from the Superior Court of Yuma County (Arizona) revoking his probations imposed following his convictions for possession of a dangerous drug, attempted sale of a dangerous drug, and theft. He asserted that the trial court erred by concluding that it was required to revoke his probations under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-917(B) with regard to his intensive probations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a dangerous drug, attempted sale of a dangerous drug, and theft. The trial court placed him on intensive probation for the first two counts, and on supervised probation on the theft count. When defendant tested positive for methamphetamine, his probation officer filed a petition to revoke the probations for violating standard condition nine, which prohibited the use of controlled substances. After a revocation hearing, the trial court found that defendant had violated his probations and, pursuant to § 13-917(B), revoked the probations and imposed prison terms. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed in part. It explained that, under § 13-917(B), once a petition was filed, the statute required revocation if a trial court found that a defendant had committed a felony offense. Here it was undisputed that defendant committed a felony. He used methamphetamine, a dangerous drug, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3401(6)(b)(xii), which was a class 4 felony, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3407(A)(1), (B)(1). The court reversed in part because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-917(B) did not apply to the supervised probation for theft. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901(C).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the order revoking defendant's intensive probations imposed for possession of a dangerous drug and attempted sale of a dangerous drug. It reversed in part the order revoking his supervised probation for theft and remanded that cause for the trial court to determine whether to revoke the probation and impose a prison term or to modify the conditions of probation.

 

779 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


1 CA-CR 95-0497


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


186 Ariz. 490; 924 P.2d 494; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 57; 213 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



March 28, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on September 24, 1996 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-96-0286-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 94-05950. The Honorable Lawrence O. Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that convicted defendant of aggravated assault and imposed the mandatory minimum sentence of five years imprisonment. The trial court, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-603(J) (renumbered as Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-603(K)), entered a special order allowing defendant to petition the Board of Executive Clemency for a commutation of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: At sentencing the trial court expressed regret that it had to impose prison time and found the sentence clearly excessive. The trial court entered a special order allowing defendant to petition for a commutation of his sentence. In support of the order, the trial court cited defendant's lack of prior felony convictions, his need for anger control counseling and treatment, and the fact that he was the father of an infant daughter. On appeal, defendant argued that the sentencing scheme was unconstitutional. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court found that the trial court had the duty to not impose a sentence that was grossly disproportionate under the Eighth Amendment. Absent such a finding, though, the trial court had no constitutional authority to impose a sentence that was any less severe than the range of sentences prescribed by the legislature. The mere fact that defendant had the additional remedy of seeking commutation of his sentence worked to his benefit. Defendant's crime was a violent crime involving the use of a deadly weapon. The court determined that a prison term of five years was not grossly disproportionate to defendant's crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated assault and the sentence imposed.

State v. Savio


1 CA-CR 95-0593


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


186 Ariz. 487; 924 P.2d 491; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 53; 212 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



March 19, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on September 24, 1996 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-96-0253-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 95-00019. The Honorable Thomas Dunevant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which upheld a trial court's conviction of defendant for the crime of manifesting an intent to solicit prostitution. Defendant contended that the ordinance under which he was charged was vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The court indicated that its review did not reveal any fundamental error. The court held that Phoenix, Ariz. Code § 23-52(a)(3) did not violate the First, Fifth, or Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution or Ariz. Const. art. II § 6. Therefore, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court found that the statute criminalized the specific act of manifesting an intent to solicit prostitution and listed behaviors that, in context, evidenced such an intent. The list was non-exclusive and allowed consideration of other behaviors, that manifested an intent to solicit prostitution. The court concluded that given the specific behavioral evidence needed to support the inference of intent, the statute was not vague. The court also reasoned that although criminalization of the isolated lawful behaviors listed in the ordinance would be unconstitutional, the ordinance did not criminalize those lawful activities in isolation from intent and context, thus the ordinance was not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that upheld a trial court's conviction of defendant for the crime of manifesting an intent to solicit prostitution.

 

781 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brockell


2 CA-CR 94-0437


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


187 Ariz. 226; 928 P.2d 650; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 40; 211 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 57



February 29, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-41866. Honorable John F. Kelly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, which dismissed an indictment charging defendant with causing criminal damage in an amount more than $ 2,000 but less than $ 10,000, a class five felony under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1602(A), (B)(2), based on its finding that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it defined the class of felony based on the amount of damage inflicted but did not specify how that amount was to be calculated. He alleged that the statute permitted an arbitrary and discriminatory application. The court disagreed. The court held that defendant could only be convicted of causing such damage as the proof would support, given properly recognized measures of damages. There were several appropriate methods of determining damages. The amount had to be determined by applying a rule of reasonableness to the particular fact situation presented. The State had the burden to establish the amount of damages, which defendant could challenge with his own more reasonable calculation. The jury would have been required to decide which was more reasonable. Thus, a conviction for criminal damage was based on the evidence presented, given generally accepted measures of damages, and not on the whim of the police, prosecutor, judge, or jury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the cause.

Phoenix Newspapers v. Purcell


1 CA-CV 94-0223


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


187 Ariz. 74; 927 P.2d 340; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 32; 210 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 44



February 22, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 92-21714. The Honorable Sherry Hutt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper challenged a finding of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment to appellee state in an action filed to declare Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 16-168(E), unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A newspaper sought a copy of the county voter registration list. The newspaper was told that it would have to comply with Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 16-168(E). The statute required that the newspaper pay for the list, on a per name basis. The cost to the newspaper would have been prohibitive. The newspaper filed an action to have the statute declared unconstitutional, as violative of Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 13, as special legislation, and against public policy. The trial court granted the state's motion for summary judgment. The newspaper appealed. As to the constitutional question, the court applied the rational basis test and found that there existed a reasonable state interest in not providing the list free of charge, which was to protect the privacy of the voters. The court also found that the statute was not "special legislation" by allowing political parties free copies while charging everyone else, in that there was a rational basis for the statute and class members could move back and forth between groups. The court finally found that public policy was not violated because the list was available to anyone, just at a cost.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted the state by the trial court.

 

783 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Prince v. City of Apache Junction


2 CA-CV 95-0170


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


185 Ariz. 43; 912 P.2d 47; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 26; 210 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 42



February 15, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY. Cause No. CV 94042204. Honorable William J. O'Neil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured person sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona), which granted defendant city's motion to dismiss the injured person's personal injury suit because it was immune from such suit pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551.


OVERVIEW: The injured person was playing softball for his company's team on a field within the city's park as part of a softball league and was injured. His company paid a fee to the city to play in the league. The trial court dismissed his cause of action. The court reversed because the injured person was not a "recreational user" as defined in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551 and the city was thus not immune from suit. The injured person was injured on a softball field during the course of an official, city-sponsored league softball game. The participation of his team and its members depended on the team's required payment of an entry fee to the city. That payment was made with the understanding that this entry fee was a requirement of entering a team into the league and to use the league facilities. Part of the entry fee was for field preparation, which included maintenance personnel dragging the field and chalking the lines and stripes and installing bases, and part of the entry fee was allocated towards the light use fee for the softball fields at night use. But for the payment of the entry fee, the injured person could not have used the softball field at the time his accident occurred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the injured person's personal injury suit against the city and remanded.

 

784 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCoy


2 CA-CR 94-0510


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


187 Ariz. 223; 928 P.2d 647; 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 23; 210 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 40



February 13, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 1197.


PRIOR HISTORY: Honorable Richard D. Nichols, Judge. Cause No. CR-44875. APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his the judgment of Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted him of participating in a criminal street gang, a class two felony, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2308(A) and (G).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction on the basis that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2308 was unconstitutionally overbroad because it regulated constitutionally protected free speech. On review, the court held that the conviction was not predicated simply on defendant's act of advising or counseling the gang as to noncriminal matters. The statute proscribed such advice only when it was given with the intent to promote or further the criminal objectives of a criminal syndicate pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-308(A)(3). Words spoken with the intent to cause the commission of a criminal act were not protected by the First Amendment. Defendant also objected to various exhibits with gang insignia on them. The court found that the writing on these exhibits was not offered to prove the truth of any of the words contained therein, but rather as evidence of the knowledge and gang participation of the possessor. For that reason, they were not hearsay, and the identity of their author was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Little v. All Phoenix S. Cmty. Mental Health Ctr.


2 CA-CV 95-0256


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


186 Ariz. 97; 919 P.2d 1368; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 288; 206 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



December 26, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY. Cause No. CV 91-23178. Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) which entered a directed verdict in favor of defendant mental health centers. In her complaint, the wife alleged that the mental health centers owed a duty, not only to her husband, their patient, but also to herself and their child. She also alleged that the mental health centers breached their duty of care by refusing to hospitalize her husband.


OVERVIEW: Following sporadic treatment by the mental health centers, their patient stabbed his wife. The mental health centers were aware that the patient had thoughts of injuring his wife, but he did not communicate any express threat of imminent serious physical harm to her. At trial, the court held that the wife had failed to establish the mental health centers' liability under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-517.02. To establish statutory liability, the wife was required to show that the patient had communicated to the mental health provider an explicit threat of imminent serious physical harm or death to a clearly identified victim. On appeal, the court agreed that the wife had not stated a valid claim under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-517.02. However, the evidence was sufficient to support a prima facie claim of liability under Arizona case law. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-517.02 unconstitutionally abrogated a general negligence cause of action for persons who were not "clearly identified" by a patient but who were foreseeable victims.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court's directed verdict, which was based solely on a statute which had unconstitutionally abrogated a cause of action, could not stand. The judgment for defendants was reversed because the wife had established a prima facie common law claim against the mental health centers for a breach of their duty to her.

State v. Jackson


1 CA-CV 94-0302


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


184 Ariz. 296; 908 P.2d 1081; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 279; 206 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



December 19, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County. Cause Nos. CR-15980 and CR-15981. The Honorable Steven F. Conn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bond company contested the order of the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona) and sought reversal of the trial court's forfeiture judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a forfeiture judgment against the bond company in a criminal case. The bond company appealed, contending that appellee government failed to comply with the statute governing forfeiture orders. The court held that the Arizona State Constitution conferred on the Arizona Supreme Court the power to make rules relative to all procedural matters in any court pursuant to Ariz. Const. art. 6, § 5(5). The rule-making power was vested in the supreme court exclusively. The court ruled that the statutory procedures under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3973 were inconsistent with procedural rules adopted by the Arizona Supreme Court in Ariz. R. Crim. P. 7.6(d). The statutory procedures therefore were unconstitutional. The court affirmed the forfeiture judgment because the trial court's failure to comply with Rule 7.6(d) did not prejudice the bond company and because the bond company had an opportunity to contest the forfeiture judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the forfeiture judgment of the trial court against the bond company.

Russo v. Catalina Foothills Unified Sch. Dist. No. 16


2 CA-CV 95-0220


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


185 Ariz. 253; 914 P.2d 1345; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 275; 205 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 55



December 14, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 306691. Honorable Bernardo P. Velasco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff resident challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which dismissed his complaint against defendant school district in the resident's action for declaratory relief.


OVERVIEW: The Arizona Supreme Court issued an opinion that held that the existing statutory school financing structure was unconstitutional because it caused gross disparities in school facilities. The supreme court clarified that opinion and held that it did not affect any bonded indebtedness that was conducted after the opinion was issued but before new school financing legislation was enacted. The resident brought suit against the school district, for declaratory relief, and sought to have the school district's bonds issued after the supreme court's opinion declared invalid. The trial court dismissed the resident's complaint and the resident appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the supreme court's clarifying order applied to all bonds issued after its opinion and before new school financing legislation was enacted. The court further held that the clarification order authorized future bond indebtedness under the existing statutes until the statutes were invalidated by legislative replacement or by future court action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which dismissed the resident's action for declaratory relief.

Kahn v. Thompson


2 CA-CV 95-0167


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


185 Ariz. 408; 916 P.2d 1124; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 267; 204 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 64



November 30, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court June 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 302825. Honorable Gilbert Veliz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee affirmative action division (division). The citizen claimed that the division violated the city's human relations ordinance when it failed to investigate his claims that discounts for senior citizens and children constituted illegal age discrimination.


OVERVIEW: The court found that price discounts were not among the prohibited acts delineated in the ordinance, so the citizen did not expressly state violations of the ordinance. The court concluded that the question of whether age-related discounts fell within the ordinance were matters involving interpretation of the ordinance, so the division was entitled to exercise its judgment and discretion in determining the scope of the ordinance since it was charged with enforcing it. The court concluded that mandamus was not available, because the division had discretion to determine whether the citizen had stated a colorable claim. The court found that prohibiting age-related discounts was not an intended objective or construction of the ordinance, so the city's establishment of numerous mandatory senior citizen discounts was a clear indication of legislative intent, as well as a reflection of widely accepted public policy. The court concluded that the age-based discounts complained of had a sufficiently rational basis, and therefore did not deny the citizen the equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

TUCSON ELEC. POWER CO. v. APACHE CTY.


1 CA-TX 93-0015


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


185 Ariz. 5; 912 P.2d 9; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 261; 204 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



November 21, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause Nos. TX 91-01595 and TX 90-01686. The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED. Opinion of the Tax Court, 175 Ariz. 485, 857 P.2d 1339 VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, utility companies, appealed the judgment of the Arizona Tax Court, which sustained the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-992(B) (1990) and applied retroactively both § 15-922(B) and amendment to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-227(A) (1990). Additionally, one utility company separately challenged the dismissal of its refund claim for its failure, while in Chapter 11 bankruptcy, to timely pay accruing Arizona real property taxes.


OVERVIEW: The utility companies contended that § 15-992(B) was constitutional and that the tax court erred in holding that the 1990 amendments to §§ 15-992(B) and 42-227(A) applied retroactively. One utility company also contended that the tax court's dismissal of its refund complaint during the pendency of its bankruptcy proceeding violated automatic stay provisions. The court held that the 1990 amendment to § 15-992(B) was an unconstitutional special law but did not address other constitutional challenges. Because the unconstitutional amendment is void, the court held that its predecessor statute, § 15-992(B)(1989), which included all assessed property in the class of taxpayers in those affected districts, was automatically revived. Although the court applied its decision retroactively, the court held that the utility companies were only entitled to a partial refund of the taxes they paid. The court held that § 42-2271(A) was properly given retroactive application. Finally, the court held that the tax court's dismissal of one utility company's claim for failure to pay a subsequently levied tax after it filed for Chapter 11 bankruptcy violated automatic stay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the tax court n part, reversed the decision of the tax court in part, and remanded.

State v. Walker


1 CA-CR 93-0057, 1 CA-CR 93-0109, 1 CA-CR 93-0362 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


185 Ariz. 228; 914 P.2d 1320; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 245; 202 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 61



November 2, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on April 23, 1996 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-96-0018-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: MARICOPA County Superior Court No. CR 91-00997. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 91-00997. The Honorable Micael D. Ryan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant senator and appellant lobbyist challenged the judgments of conviction entered against them by the Superior Court of Maricopa County ( Arizona) for filing a false campaign contribution statement and conspiracy and bribery respectively.


OVERVIEW: Appellant senator and appellant lobbyist were captured on audio and video tape during a sting operation to uncover corruption. They challenged their convictions for filing a false campaign contribution statement and conspiracy and bribery charges respectively. Both claimed that their cases should have been dismissed because, inter alia, the undercover informant deliberately destroyed material evidence, namely, the notes of the author who had interviewed him and written a book about the investigation. Appellants asserted that the destruction of the evidence violated their right to due process of law under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 4. The court rejected the argument, stating that the potential evidence lost because of the alleged destruction of the notes did not warrant dismissal as the evidence was cumulative impeachment evidence. Appellants made no showing that the notes might have contained information not otherwise available to them. Thus the trial court correctly concluded that the notes were not constitutionally material and that the destruction of the notes did not violate appellants' constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed, because the destruction of notes which were found to be cumulative impeachment evidence did not violate appellants' constitutional rights.

STATE v. HUMMER


2 CA-CR 93-0596


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted him of two counts of sexual conduct with a minor, three counts of furnishing obscene material to a minor, and one count of molestation of a minor. He had two prior felony convictions and was sentenced to three consecutive life terms on the sexual conduct and molestation charges and concurrent sentences of 12 years on the obscene material charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in August 1992, after more than one year of sexual behavior with four boys. At trial, two brothers, both minors, testified to several instances in which defendant had engaged in sexual behavior with them. The brothers and a minor friend, who lived in the same trailer park as defendant, described the sexual acts and testified that defendant had made them watch pornographic videos while he masturbated. Defendant then moved to another trailer park and engaged in sexual conduct with another minor. He was convicted of sexual conduct with a minor, molestation, and furnishing obscene material to minors. The court found that under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3501(1)(a), to convict defendant of furnishing obscene or harmful material to minors, the jury had to apply contemporary state standards with respect to what was suitable for minors. The court reasoned that expert testimony was only appropriate when the trier of fact could not understand the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of sexual conduct with a minor, furnishing obscene material to a minor, and molestation of a minor.

State v. Baldwin


1 CA-CR 94-0464


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


184 Ariz. 267; 908 P.2d 483; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 234; 202 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



October 24, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 18, 1996. Counsel Amended January 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 93-00770. The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which upheld her conviction in the municipal court for residential picketing, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2909. She was sentenced to five days in jail, a $ 210.00 fine, and one year of probation. Defendant was walking back and forth, carrying a bible and praying aloud in front of the home of a doctor whose practice included abortions.


OVERVIEW: The court construed Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2909 as prohibiting only focused picketing taking place solely in front of a particular residence; therefore, the statute was not overbroad and violative of the First Amendment in that context. The court found that whether or not defendant ranged at times beyond the doctor's home, the evidence permitted the conclusion that she targeted his home. The court found that in the context of a prohibition against targeted residential picketing, the term "picket" had a singular, commonly understood meaning and thus was not vague. The court found that the term "demonstrates" gave adequate notice of the conduct that § 13-2909 proscribed. Thus, the court found that § 13-2909 was not void for vagueness. The court found that the state imposed reasonable restrictions on the time, place, and manner of speech: § 13-2909 was content-neutral, § 13-2909 left open ample alternate channels of communication, and § 13-2909 served a significant government interest of protecting residential privacy. The court affirmed and concluded that the statute did not single out religious "picketing" or "demonstrations" for prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court upholding defendant's conviction for residential picketing.
