State v. Stine


1 CA-CR 95-0128-PR


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


184 Ariz. 1; 906 P.2d 58; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 230; 201 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 48



October 19, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Rule 32.9(c), Arizona Rules of Criminal Procedure). Cause Nos. CR 91-00168. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVIEW GRANTED; RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for review of the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which summarily dismissed her petition for post-conviction relief. The trial court found no merit to defendant's claim that she was entitled to be eligible for commutation of her sentence under a recent amendment to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the portion of the amended sentencing statute that allowed for sentence commutation was a significant change in the law that should be given retroactive effect. Defendant requested a "surgically precise" application of the amendment provision because application of the entire amended statute would have eliminated her parole eligibility in violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause, U.S. Const. art. I., § 10, cl. 1. On appeal, the court held that criminals are sentenced under the law in effect when the crime was committed. The court noted that Arizona statutes were not given retroactive effect unless the legislature clearly evinced such an intention, and held that in this case, the legislature clearly indicated in 1993 Ariz. Sess. Laws, ch. 255, §§ 99 and 101 that the amendment operated prospectively. The court also held that the parole non-eligibility provision did not offend the executive powers of clemency under Ariz. Const. art. 5, § 5. The court rejected an argument that defendant was entitled to equitable relief and found that defendant was not eligible for parity review by the Board of Executive Clemency.


OUTCOME: The court granted review of the order of the trial court that summarily denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, but the court denied relief.

 

794 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. CURTIS


1 CA-CR 95-0030 PR


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


185 Ariz. 112; 912 P.2d 1341; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 208; 199 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



September 12, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review from the Superior Court of Mohave County (Rule 32.9(c), Arizona Rules of Criminal Procedure). Cause No. CR-9762. The Honorable Steven F. Conn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Review Granted; Relief Denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona), which denied his second petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of sexual assault. His appeal and his first post-conviction relief petition were denied. He filed a second petition, which the trial court also denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. When it dismissed the prisoner's petition without awaiting the state's response, the trial court was able to consider preclusion pursuant to Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32.2(a)(2), (3). Because the prisoner had raised issues of ineffective assistance of counsel in his appeal and his first post-conviction relief petition, the prisoner had already had the benefit of an evidentiary hearing at which the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel had been explored. Although the prisoner claimed that the alibi instruction given at his trial was constitutionally infirm, he had not raised the issue previously, and the issue lacked sufficient constitutional magnitude to justify the prisoner's belated focus. The trial court had already held that the prisoner had not been entitled to a sexual abuse instruction. The prisoner could not argue that his earlier failure to raise these claims was due to ineffective assistance of counsel. Such an argument would have created an infinite regression.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to deny post-conviction relief.

 

795 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Williams-Carter v. Maricopa County


2 CA-CV 95-0148


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


183 Ariz. 338; 903 P.2d 646; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 207; 198 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 40



September 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY. Cause No. CV92-13111. Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of a grant of summary judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) in favor of appellee county in the applicant's suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, which alleged that her U.S. Const. amend. I rights were violated when the county refused to consider her for the position of clerk of the county's Board of Supervisors (the board) based on her political affiliation.


OVERVIEW: The applicant was a registered Democrat employed as clerk of another county's board of supervisors. Although the applicant met the announced position requirements, was otherwise qualified for the job, and was included on a short list of 16 candidates out of 190 applicants, she was denied an interview because of her political affiliation. The trial court held that it was not discriminatory to require that the position of clerk be held by a person registered with the political party of the board's choosing and the court affirmed that decision. The court held that patronage hiring of public employees was permissible when the employee would hold a policymaking decision. The court found that the clerk position was a policymaking position based on the clerk's right to cast votes for a replacement supervisor in the event of a vacancy and the clerk's attendance at confidential meetings of the board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the county's motion for summary judgment.

 

796 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Scottsdale Princess Pshp. v. Maricopa County


1 CA-TX 93-0016


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


185 Ariz. 368; 916 P.2d 1084; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 194; 197 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 57



August 24, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on May 21, 1996 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0546-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 90-00308 (Consolidated). The Honorable William J. Schafer III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The taxpayer challenged the decision of the Arizona Tax Court that sustained the legality of property tax assessments on its parcels and improvements. The county challenged the determination that the taxpayer could not be held liable for additional taxes resulting from the transfer of improvements from the unsecured to the secured roll. The Department of Revenue challenged the order assessing it for failing to comply Ariz. R. Civ. P. Rule 26.1.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer claimed that because its improvements to the real estate were improperly assessed on the unsecured roll, it was entitled to a full refund of all taxes paid as a result of the assessment. The county argued that it was error to fail to require the taxpayer to pay the additional taxes accrued when the improvements were transferred from the unsecured roll to the secured roll, and the Department of Revenue argued that it was improper to assess it penalties for failing to comply with mandatory discovery. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court concluded that the taxpayer was not entitled to a full refund merely because of an incorrect assessment. Instead, the court held that the taxpayer was entitled to a refund if any excess taxes had been paid. The court found no authority in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-204 which would have permitted the county to be awarded the additional taxes that accrued when the improvements were transferred to the secured roll. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the finding that the Department of Revenue violated Ariz. R. Civ. P. 26.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the legality of the assessments on the taxpayer's property and improvements, affirmed the determination that the taxpayer was not liable for the additional taxes resulting when his improvements were transferred from the unsecured to the secured roll, and reversed the assessment of attorney fees and costs against the Department of Revenue and remanded for an assessment of reasonable attorney fees and expenses.

 

797 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Bird v. State


1 CA-CV 94-0010


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


184 Ariz. 198; 908 P.2d 12; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 187; 197 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



August 22, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on December 19, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0437-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County. Cause No. CV 993-0148. The Honorable Richard Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which dismissed the charges against defendant under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 16-1015 for wagering on the outcome of an election based on the trial court's finding that § 16-1015 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with violations of § 16-1015 for wagering on the outcome of an election after such wager between defendants appeared as a public announcement in a newspaper. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the charges that the trial court denied. Defendants filed a petition for special action with the appellate court. The appellate court dismissed the charges and held that § 16-1015 was unconstitutional. On further appeal, the court held that § 16-1015 was not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. It was not vague on its face because the words were understandable by people of ordinary intelligence who, therefore, had notice of the prohibited conduct, and law enforcement officials were given guidelines for enforcement. Section 16-1015 did not infringe on defendants' right to free speech because the wager was not a particularized message nor was there a great likelihood that the message would be understood by those who viewed it. The statute sought to punish conduct, had only an incidental affect on free speech, and restricted free speech no greater than what was essential to further the substantial governmental interest of regulating gambling.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court that found the statute that prohibited wagering on the outcome of elections to be unconstitutional.

 

798 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re United States Currency in the Amount of $ 315,900.00


2 CA-CV 94-0196


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


183 Ariz. 208; 902 P.2d 351; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 195; 197 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



August 22, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 292768. Honorable William H. Tinney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which forfeited to the state government an amount of currency that was found within defendant's vehicle in close proximity to illegal drugs.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant's vehicle after he observed it speeding. The officer smelled an odor of marijuana and found a bag of marijuana and a box of currency totaling $ 313,500 in the vehicle. Defendant pleaded guilty to unlawful possession of marijuana weighing less than one pound. The trial court forfeited the amount of currency to the state. The court held that, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4311(K), the government had the initial burden of demonstrating probable cause for forfeiture. Here, the government did not demonstrate reasonable grounds for its belief that the property was subject to forfeiture. The statutory inference of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4305(B), that money found in proximity to contraband was used in the commission of the offense, was insufficient by itself to establish probable cause. There was no additional evidence connecting the currency to any criminal activity. Thus, the court held that the statutory inference of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4305(B) was but one factor that might be considered in determining probable cause for seizure and for forfeiture. A determination of probable cause which rested solely on the inference was constitutionally impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions to dismiss the case with prejudice. The government's evidence was constitutionally inadequate to support a finding of probable cause for forfeiture of the currency found in defendant's vehicle.

 

799 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Van Riper v. Threadgill


1 CA-CV 95-0195


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


183 Ariz. 580; 905 P.2d 589; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 186; 197 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



August 17, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on November 21, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0438-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 94-16614. The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff resident challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted defendant town's motion for summary judgment, ruling that the failure to file the statement of organization invalidated the signatures because the circulator of the petition failed to identify himself and his organization. The resident had sought to compel the town clerk to submit the signatures to the county recorder for verification.


OVERVIEW: The resident sought to have a zoning issue referred to the voters. After the resident submitted the petition signature sheets, the town clerk refused to transmit them to the county recorder for verification because the sheets contained 10, rather than 15, signature lines and because the resident had not submitted the statement of organization form before he and others collected the signatures. The trial court granted the town's motion for summary judgment, ruling that the failure to file the statement of organization invalidated the signatures. The trial court also ruled that the fact that the signature sheets contained 10 signature lines rather than 15 lines was not a sufficient reason to invalidate the petitions. On appeal, the court reversed. The court determined that although the resident and his group were a political committee within the definition of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 16-901(15), the statutes and the forms supplied to applicants are so confusing that they set a trap for those who are trying to exercise their right to seek a referendum. The trial court correctly held that the petition was not defective because the forms contained only 10 rather than 15 signature lines.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court with respect to the issue whether the petition was defective because no statement of organization was filed. The court remanded to the trial court with directions to enter an order granting summary judgment to the resident and directing the town clerk to forward the referendum petition to the Maricopa County Recorder for processing. Finally, the court awarded attorney's fees to the resident.

 

800 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Fry's Food Stores v. Mather & Assocs.


1 CA-CV 92-0335, 1 CA-CV 93-0505 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


183 Ariz. 89; 900 P.2d 1225; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 169; 196 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



August 3, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 91-18769. The Honorable Michael O. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) dismissed plaintiff property owners' negligence action against defendants, architect, structural engineer, general contractor, and subcontractor, as barred by the construction statute of limitations, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-552. The trial court also awarded attorney's fees against the property owners under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-341.01(A). The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed a negligence action against the architect, structural engineer, general contractor, and subcontractor, when the canopy to their building blew off in a windstorm causing extensive exterior and interior damage. The trial court dismissed the action as being barred by the construction statute of repose, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-552. On appeal, the court found that by its plain terms, § 12-552 applied only to contract actions and not to negligence actions. Thus, § 12-552's eight-year limitations period did not apply to bar the action. The court found that application of § 12-552 to the property owners' negligence action would have rendered the statute unconstitutional because it would have abrogated the property owners' cause of action in violation of Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6. The court also found that because the legislature did not expressly provide that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-552 preempted tort claims, it should not have been construed as preempting the property owners' negligence action. The court also found that attorney's fees were not available under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-341.01(A) because that statute applied only to contract actions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of dismissal and reversed the award of attorney's fees against the property owners.
